management.
69.    Lengthening debt maturity is important for two reasons: first, to reduce exposure to short-
term interest rate fluctuations and second to reduce the rollover risk. In recent years, the
govemment managed to extend maturity and duration, but did so by issuing longer-term debt
linked to the dollar or indexed to the SELIC rate. Thus one problem of public debt composition
was replaced with another.
70.    The process of maturity and duration extension will be effectively limited by the slope of
the yield curve. Generally the yield curve becomes steeper in turbulent times. Brazilian
authorities were successful in flattening the term structure of interest rates after the contagion
from Argentina, but uncertainty arising from the electoral process again steepened it in late 2002.
The periods of flattening of the yield curve have been short and sporadic. As a consequence, a
market for long-dated Real-denominated securities does not exist beyond the 24 months horizon.
Over time, debt managers will have to gradually rebalance the relative weights of financial cost
vs. longer maturities, and accept the higher cost of issuing instruments with lesser risk for public
finances.
71.    The lengthening of maturity and duration requires building a liquid market for debt at all
maturities. The secondary market for government paper (for delivery) is very illiquid compared
to both the repo and derivatives markets. The repo market can only provide transitory liquidity,
and hence, cannot be a permanent source of liquidity for govemment securities holders.
72.    The derivatives and repo markets have drained much of the liquidity from the cash
markets (and from secondary markets for delivery), because these transactions are not subject to
22 Garcia, M. (2002) Public Debt Management, Monetary Policy and Financial Institutions. Background Paper for
World Bank Country Economic Memorandum, Brazil. Washington, D.C.
22



reserve requirements or the debit tax (Contribuiq&o Provis6ria sobre Movimentaqfo Financeira
or CPMF). Additionally, until very recently, repos, futures, and swaps were not considered fixed
income securities, and as such were subject to quarterly income or capital gains taxes as opposed
to monthly taxes as in the case of cash fixed income instruments. All of these considerations
discourage securities trading in the cash market and hence inhibit the development of a
secondary market for government debt.
73.    Improving the liquidity of the government bond market requires liquidity in money
markets, as they reduce liquidity risks for bondholders that want access to cash. Brazilian money
markets (besides the Repo one) are illiquid, and several analysts see the CPMF taxation as one of
the causes.23  Other studies find that, generally, in emerging economies, high reserve
requirements represent one of the reasons for the lack of depth of money markets.24  Higher
reserve requirements tend to make banks' demand for reserves more stable and less sensitive to
interest rate fluctuations. Hence banks cannot play an active role in smoothing market liquidity
shortages. In effect, evidence for Brazil shows that reserves do not respond to interest rates
(Central Bank of Brazil, 1998). Hence, coordination of monetary policy and public debt
management is a critical issue in developing a long term market for government bonds.
74.    Besides short maturity, another crucial feature of Brazilian debt is the high degree of
indexation. Indexation is a substitute for credibility, albeit very imperfect. In Brazil, most of the
indexation is to the Selic or to the exchange rate (Table 8). Indexation to the Selic rate runs the
risk of reducing the effectiveness of monetary policy. Indexation to the exchange rate may lead
to the reluctance on the part of the monetary authorities to let the currency float for fear of its
negative effects on the debt level.

75.    The issuing of price-indexed debt would enhance the credibility of monetary policy. Not
only would this impose costs on the sovereign of generating inflation, but it may provide useful
information  to the- monetary   authorities  on  inflation  expectations.  However, this
recommendation has its practical limitations, as the amount of these type of securities in the total
23 Glaessner, T (2002) Notes on Brazilian Capital Markets. Mimeo. World Bank.
24 Mohanty, M. S. (2002) Improving liquidity in government bond markets: What can be done?. BIS. www.bis.org.
23



portfolio is bound to a certain extent by the market's demand and other institutional
characteristics.25 In most countries that issue this type of instrument, its share does not exceed 20
percent of total, with the exception of Israel, Chile and Mexico. Hence, the best solution to build
credibility is to establish an independent Central Bank in conjunction with sound macroeconomic
management. Without enough credibility, the slope of the yield curve will make the cost of
maturity extension prohibitive.
b. Government Actions: Achievements and Challenges
76.   Brazil has made good progress in the area of public debt management, particularly
extending debt maturity and duration (Figure 3) thanks to the stabilization of the economy and to
institutional developments that led to more transparent and efficient debt markets. And yet,
despite the significant accomplishments, public debt management continues to pose major
challenges related to the short debt duration and its high degree of indexation.
77.   Besides sound macroeconomic fundamentals management (i.e. primary surplus,
credibility in anti-inflationary policy), the portfolio composition transition process involves a
market development strategy. Brazil has already initiated this institution-building process by
strengthening STN operations, formulating and disseminating annual borrowing plans,
developing the auctions markets, and introducing limited repo markets. In collaboration with the
Bank, authorities are working on measures to achieve further progress in capital markets
development.
78.   Over the last few years, the Government has developed and started to implement an
agenda for institutional reform of the internal governance arrangements for federal public debt
management and for strengthening debt management capacities in the STN. Steady and
considerable progress has been achieved in building STN's debt management capacity. The
newly created Middle Office has been producing regular, high quality reports on the debt
portfolio and STN operations. It has been working to upgrade its information technology
systems, and developing its capacity to handle a new risk management model with Bank
technical assistance. The STN presently publishes annual borrowing plans, which include debt
portfolio benchmarks, as well as an internal medium-term debt strategy document.
79.   The Government was also planning to move more decisively in clarifying the respective
roles of agencies involved in public debt management. The main objective was to either unify
all debt management operations in the STN, or to develop a formal coordination mechanism
between the STN and the Central Bank so as to ensure the application of a single, coherent debt
management strategy to guide both domestic and external debt operations. However, given the
uncertainty and volatility in the external environment, the government postponed this decision to
avoid possible negative market reactions to a new arrangement whose impacts were somewhat
uncertain at least in the short run.  Thus, clarifying and strengthening the governance
arrangement remains a pending task on the institutional development front.
75 For instance, in the United States the relatively lackluster performance by Treasury Inflation-Indexed Securities
(TIIS) is explained by several factors: concentration on the TUS market, reduced liquidity of the instruments and
difficulties associated with launching a new instrument. (Sack, B. and R. Elsasser. 2002. "Treasury Inflation-
Indexed Debt: A Review of the U.S. Experience." Federal Reserve Board of Governors Discussion Paper. June.
24



80.   Although authorities succeeded in developing the debt portfolio management model and
announced strategies through their Annual Financing Plans in 2001 and 2002, debt managers, in
their desire to reduce financial costs, accepted increased exchange rate and roll-over risks. The
general direction of the debt management strategy (increasing maturity and duration, reducing
rollover risk, reducing indexation to Selic rates and to the exchange rate), as reflected in the
Annual Borrowing Plan targets (see Annex on Public Debt Management) is appropriate to reduce
Brazil's vulnerability to shocks. However, the observed debt composition still diverges from the
targets. While part of the explanation for the missed targets is due to market conditions outside
the Government's control, a remaining part of the explanation is the institutional shortcomings
that lead debt managers during turbulent periods to react "opportunistically" in the sense of
issuing what the market demands, regardless of the cost/risk tradeoff of the long term strategy.
81.   Besides developing a governance structure more conducive to maintaining a long-term
strategy even during turbulent periods (see Annex on Public Debt Management), the
Government is also working on development of a market for government securities. The
development of a market for government securities is essential to implement the desired debt
composition. The Government's action plan focuses on three key and complementary strategic
dimensions: (i) designing and implementing a more explicit short- and medium-term domestic
debt issuance strategy (necessary to enhance transparency and predictability); (ii) broadening the
institutional and retail investor base and increasing its diversity (necessary to enhance demand in
the primary market); and (iii) fostering greater liquidity in local secondary markets for
government debt.
82.   As regards the development of a more explicit and predictable debt issuance program, as
outlined in the Annual Borrowing Plans, the Government is setting target ranges explicitly aimed
at reducing the proportion of dollar-linked and SELIC-indexed debt issued. To reinforce this
strategy, the Front Office of the Debt Management Office will develop a detailed short- and
medium-term domestic debt issuance program, consistent with the debt management objectives.
The implementation of such an issuance program should lead to the gradual establishment of
more liquid benchmarks - and an associated yield curve. In particular, STN will develop a
program for the regular issuance of plain-vanilla Treasury Bills (LTNs), which would anchor the
short end of the yield curve. As the objective is also to extend the duration of government debt
in a prudent manner, STN will rely on the issuance of fixed interest rate, Reais-denominated
bonds and inflation-indexed bonds to develop the medium and longer segments of the yield
curve, respectively. As debt duration is extended, complementary actions related to money and
derivative markets and to the structure of end investors will be needed, so that the transfer of risk
from the government debt portfolio to market participants can be prudently managed.
83.   The government also aims to improve the structure and resilience of the end-investor
base, necessary to enhance the primary market for government paper and support the
development of a reliable government debt yield curve. The events of last year, where massive
redemptions of mutual funds dramatically magnified asset price volatility, highlight the need to
increase the transparency of the institutional investors (particularly mutual funds) to disclose and
manage risk. In particular, problems arose from the lack of precise definitions of different types
of funds, in terms of investment policies and risks being assumed, as many funds advertised as
money market funds (where investments are not significantly exposed to the risk of capital
25



losses) took positions in longer-duration instruments that made capital losses in the midst of
financial turbulence.
84.   Authorities plan to address this problem in the context of the recent transfer of the
mandate and powers to regulate and supervise mutual funds (equity and debt) to the CVM. To
support this process, CVM and the Central Bank subscribed a Memorandum of Understanding
designed to explicitly share supervisory resources. In this area the ideal work plan would include
the development of a new regulatory framework for equity and fixed-income funds (including
hedge funds). This will involve: (i) a better demarcation of the types of funds; (ii) a clear
specification of the rights and obligations of fund investors and managers; and (iii) improved
disclosure requirements, especially of the risks associated with individual fund investment
policies. At the same time, a robust valuation framework needs to be developed, which would
enable more reliable market valuation of securities held by funds and more meaningful fund
performance measurement.
85.   STN also intends to broaden the investor base and increase competition for savings
products by further developing the Treasury Direct system that allows retail investors to buy
government securities over the internet. To this end, STN will initiate a marketing/investor
outreach campaign, and improve the connectivity of the Treasury Direct system with the systems
of participating banks. Finally, the Government will explore avenues to allow a broader group of
institutions to distribute government securities through linkages to the Treasury Direct System.
B.    TOWARDS A MORE EFFICIENT TAx SYSTEM
a. Background and Issues
86.   Tax reform constitutes another critical area of reform for sustainability of fiscal
adjustment. The commendable achievements of the primary surplus targets so far have been
made largely via revenue enhancement rather than expenditure reduction. Both the federal and
state governments have generally been quite effective in raising tax revenues over the past few
years, and some of the gains are due to improved efficiency of tax administration thanks to
modernization efforts.
87.   However, the positive performance at both levels masks underlying problems that require
attention. At the federal level, the problem arises from the types of tax instruments used to raise
additional revenues. Given Brazil's particular fiscal federalism arrangement, which assigns the
most efficient tax revenue instrument, the Goods and Services Tax (ICMS), to the states, the
Federal Government has had to resort to a series of distortionary taxes on payroll, turnover, and
financial transactions to meet revenue targets. While empirical evidence is hard to gather, there
is broad based recognition that this has imposed a significant cost in terms of the efficiency of
the national economy.
88.   Roughly 40 percent of federal tax revenues has come from the turnover taxes PIS/PASEP
(Contribui,do para Programa de Integra,cdo Social), COFINS (Contribui,do para o
Financiamento da Seguridade Social), and CPMF (Contribui,do Provis6ria sobre
Movimenta,dcao Financeira). These indirect cascading taxes were created to make up for the
financing gap created by the entitlement expenditures in the social security and assistance
26



programs. As cumulative taxes, their burden varies across sectors and across enterprises, leading
to large distortions in relative prices and inefficiencies.
89.   Payroll taxes, including Social Security contributions (RGPS), the saldrio educa.do, and
various sector-specific taxes earmarked for apprenticeship programs and other worker benefits
capped under the S-System, account for slightly over 25 percent of federal revenue. While
important as a source of government revenue, these taxes add to the cost of labor in the formal
sector, and create an incentive to operate informally, resulting in losses in terms of scale
economies, access to credit markets, and other benefits that accompany formal sector
employment.
90.    At the state level, the issue is the lack of uniformity in regulating and administering the
ICMS and its limited base. Each state sets its own ICMS rates with its own legislation. This has
resulted in a chaotic situation with, currently, 44 disparate rates in the country. The potential for
discretion has resulted in states engaging in so-called fiscal wars, or the competitive granting of
fiscal incentives to lure private investors, with negative effects on revenue collection.26 To
compensate for the loss of revenue from the fiscal incentives conceded to attract investments,
states impose high rates on relatively immobile bases such as public utilities services, in
particular electricity and telecommunication. There is a vicious cycle between the fiscal war on
the one hand and the further concentration of the ICMS tax base, with the two sources of revenue
vulnerability reinforcing each other to prevent enhancement of the states' revenue collection
capacities.
91.    Local government taxation faces at least two problems.  The first is the under-
exploitation of the property tax base. The second is the municipal tax on services ISS (Imposto
Sobre Serviqos), which is clearly a cascading tax that adversely effects the competitiveness of
sectors where production is intensive in services and, like the state ICMS, is subject to a tax war
competition among municipalities.
b. GovernmentAction: AchievementsandChallenges
92.    Despite the general consensus on the nature of systemic weaknesses, tax reform has
encountered enormous political opposition, and progress has been disappointing. The main
reasons for the tax reform deadlock in'recent years were attributable to: (i) uncertainty regarding
the fiscal revenue effects; (ii) the dependence of tax reform on a broader fiscal reform agenda -
especially social security reform and the alleviation of expenditure rigidity; and (iii) the
constraints imposed by the complex fiscal federalism structure.
93.    Since 1995, there have only been a few minor improvements to Brazil's tax system, such
as the 1996 exemption of exports from the federal cumulative taxation and the state ICMS tax.
The evident political difficulty faced by the recent tax reform proposals reform led many
observers, including the IMF and the Bank, to judge that a prospect for a major tax reform was
low at least in the short run.
26 In some cases, these fiscal incentives appear to function as defacto industrial subsidies, sustaining firms which
might not otherwise be capable of staying alive for lack of competitiveness.
27



94.   Since then, however, the political climate surrounding this issue has changed
dramatically. In 2002, the previous government issued Presidential decree MP-66 (Medida
Provis6ria, MP-66) which was later approved as Law 10.637, and initiated a modest step to
transform the small turnover PIS/PASEP into a value-added tax. The decree also contemplated a
similar reform for the larger COFINS cumulative tax for 2004. With the arrival of the new
administration, which advocated a major reshuffling of the tax system, tax reform has become
one of two major structural reform agenda being vigorously debated in the country. After broad
consultations with key stakeholders such as state governors, the private sector, labor unions as
well as at the Social and Economic Development Council, a presidential advisory board, the
Government submitted a reform proposal in the form of the Proposal for a Constitutional
Amendment (PEC) no. 41/03. The main content of the reform proposal is as follows:
o  Creation of national legislation requiring the ICMS to be imposed in a uniform manner
(with uniform rates applied) across states to avoid fiscal "wars", although states would
continue to administer the tax. The national legislation would have 5 rates and introduce
a progressivity bias with respect to the definition of these rates (lowest rate for goods of
the basic consumption basket);
o Establishment of the origin principle for the collection of ICMS on interstate trade, but
with the sharing of revenues between origin and destination states preserved;
o  Creation of a national fund for regional development, financed with 2% of the revenue
from the Income Tax (IRPF and IRPJ) and the Industrialized Goods Tax (IPI), for
allocation in the least developed regions of the country, as defined in law;
o Gradual transformation of the COFINS tax base from turnover to value-added (already
defined in the Law 10.637 of December 2002);
o  Definition of CPMF as a permanent tax with rates varying from 0.38% to 0.08%;
o  Regulation of the Federal Tax on Fortunes (IGF) by ordinary law in order to allow
flexibility to be used in the strengthening of its progressive nature;
o  Increase in the progressive nature of the state inheritance tax (ITCD);
o  Increase in the progressive nature of the municipal real state tax (ITBI-IV);
o Transfer of the federal tax on Rural Property (ITR) to the states, with rules regarding its
distribution to municipal governments to be defined by complementary law; and
o  Partial replacement of the payroll tax, used to finance the social security system for
private workers, with a turnover or non cumulative revenue tax to be defined in law: this
measure would have a mix impact on the soundness of Brazil's public finance - on the
one hand, reduction in the weight of the payroll tax would reduce economic distortions
primarily in the labor market; on the other hand, de-linking social security contributions
from the payroll could undermine the notion of the social security as a public social
insurance scheme funded with beneficiary contributions.
28



95.   On April 30, 2003, the Government submitted to Congress a proposal including the six
points listed above. In the medium term the expected outcome would be the establishment of a
simpler tax system in Brazil, in particular ICMS legislation unified across the 27 states, with five
tax rates at the most.
96.   The tax reform proposal is expected to be revenue neutral in the medium term, while in
the longer run the efficiency gains derived from a less complex system and the end of fiscal wars
among states will lead to a less burdensome tax structure that will be conducive to growth. In
particular, in the short run, to compensate for the tax base reduction implicit in switching from a
turnover-based PIS-PASEP to a value added tax, the rate was increased from 0.65% to 1.65%.
And the COFINS tax, another turnover tax (with a current base rate of 3 %), is expected to be
increased to maintain revenue neutrality. The CPMF rate reduction will begin to be implemented
only when alternative deficit-neutral options are identified. For all of the above, the tax reform
proposal is considered compatible with the medium term objective of ensuring debt
sustainability.
97.   The tax reform is also expected to have a positive impact on income distribution through
two channels. First, the reduction in indirect cumulative taxation would reduce the tax burden of
the poor. Second, the proposal introduces additional progressivity in the system of direct
taxation with the increase in the progressive nature of the state inheritance tax (ITCD) and the
municipal real estate tax (ITBI-IV), and with the regulation of Federal Tax on Fortunes (IGF) by
ordinary law which would allow flexibility to be used in the strengthening of its progressive
nature. However, the total effects would be limited as these direct taxes account for only a small
fraction of the total tax burden.
c. Modernization of Tax Administration
98.   Clearly, improvements in tax administration efficiency were key to the impressive
increase in tax revenue. In recent years, modernization of the tax collection apparatus has had
two major effects: (i) a decrease in tax evasion; and (ii) a reduction in the administrative costs
of taxation for both government and for contributors. Given limited Bank expertise in Brazil's
tax administration, the Bank team is currently conducting an expert assessment with a view to
considering inclusion in the proposed program and the loan. The most important advances in
tax administration have centered on the income tax system. In this area, Brazil has made
important progress in employing information technology resources for tax collection (i.e.,
especially for purposes of cross-checking information from different taxes and reducing the
incentives for evasion). For example, CPMF is being used as an important anti-evasion tool
through cross-checking of bank information and income tax declarations.
99.   On the contributor side, the increased effectiveness of tax administration and the
reduction of costs associated with the declaration and payment of taxes explain the increase in
the number of contributors. The definition of a comprehensive base and streamlined rate
structure of the personal income tax, together with the elimination of the indexation mechanism,
simplified the declaration and collection procedures. Both measures led to an increase in income
tax contributors from 4.4 million in 1999 to 5.2 million in 2001.
29



100.  On the corporate side, interest income was included in the base for the corporate income
tax. A much-improved treatment of transfer pricing placing Brazil in the ranks of international
best practice, coupled with the establishment of the SIMPLES27 taxation regime for micro-
enterprises, were the most important achievements in this area.
101.  The Revenue Office also reduced the time to refund excess credits to three months in
response to business sector and exporter demands for quicker credit devolution under the federal
value-added tax (IPI).
C.    EFFICIENT AND EQUITABLE PUBLIC EXPENDITURES28
102.  Improving expenditure efficiency, reach and targeting to achieve greater social impact
with the limited resources has become a key challenge and priority of the new administration.
To achieve better quality of public expenditures in terms of efficiency and equity with which
they are allocated and executed would comprise a broad and ambitious agenda of structural and
institutional reforms to be tackled over the medium term. The previous administration initiated
bold reforms of the federal public administration (e.g., Plano Diretor da Reforma do Estado) and
developed a results-oriented federal planning framework (PPA). The new administration has
placed even greater emphasis on the quality of public spending, and the Ministry of Planning,
Budget and Management (MPOG) has been developing a program to improve expenditure
efficiency (Programa de Gestdo de Custo), with links to other ongoing initiatives such as
government procurement reform, the debureaucratization program and E-government initiatives
geared to improving administrative efficiency, and efforts to institutionalize systematic program
impact evaluations.
1. Problems of Budget Rigidity
103.  Among the most difficult structural barriers to efficient allocation of budgetary resources
in Brazil is the high degree of budget rigidity. Many of the sources of this rigidity are found in
the 1988 Constitution and other legal instruments. TWe 1998 Constitution established a revenue
sharing arrangement whereby states and municipalities would share 18% and 20%, respectively,
of the federal income and industrial products taxes, and specified that these shares should
increase to 21.5%  and 22.5%, respectively, by 1993.  The Constitution and subsequent
amendments also mandated spending on certain social expenditures (notably education and
health) at specific levels of revenue or expenditures. Other legal measures have designated
various social entitlement programs (e.g., social security, unemployment insurance) as obligatory
and not subject to downward adjustment for the purposes of fiscal adjustment or resource re-
allocations. These arrangements created a highly rigid budget. Given that Brazil's public
spending already accounts for a higher share of its GDP than in most middle-income countries,
additional increases in either primary surpluses or increased social spending would have to come
from reallocation of available total resources. However, this would require a series of difficult
structural reforms to reduce budget rigidity, and accompanying measures to improve efficiency
and targeting of these expenditures. The Government has attempted to reduce the rigidity by de-
27 SIMPLES is the Sistema Integrado de Pagamento de Impostos e Contribui,ces das Microempresas e das
Empresas de Pequeno Porte
28 This is a partial description of the Government initiatives relevant to the goal of greater efficiency and equity in
public expenditures based on the available information.
30



linking part of the earmarked federal tax revenues (equivalent to about 13% of GDP); the amount
of revenues subject to earmarking was reduced by 20% in mid 1997, in a temporary measure that
has since been extended twice. In the latest renewal, the arrangement was modified to exclude
the constitutional transfers to the states and the municipalities from de-linking of the earmarked
fiscal revenues, under the rubric of Desvinculaqao de Receitas da Unido (DRU).29
104.  Maintenance of DRU would be an important short-term measure as it gives the Federal
Government a degree of expenditure flexibility to facilitate fiscal adjustments, and eventually to
improve efficiency of public expenditures. An extension of DRU alone, however, would not
sufficient to reduce expenditure rigidity in a sustainable manner. It is thus imperative for the
government to pursue structural reforms that reduce the weight of the inefficient and/or
regressive expenditures that consume large shares of the public sector budgets.  Pension
payments, which in Brazil, have notoriously regressive impacts, are a prime example of such
expenditures.  A more fundamental review  of the revenue and expenditure earmarking
arrangements beyond DRU. would also be worth considering. If the new government fails to
tackle this reform agenda, the sustainability of the gains achieved so far could be jeopardized. A
clear example is the compliance with the LRF personnel expenditure ceiling at the sub-national
level, which, without a fundamental reform of the pension system at the Federal Constitutional
level and corresponding measures at the state level, would be threatened by the ever-increasing
weight of the social security bill.
2. The Multi-annual Plan (PPA)
105.  The Brazilian Constitution mandates each government in the federation to prepare a
multi-annual plan (PPA) for its four-year term. The PPA spans the second year of the incoming
administration - because a new PPA is prepared during the government's first year in office -
and the first year of the next administration. The Constitution requires that every budget
expenditure should be included in the PPA. The introduction of a new PPA framework by the
previous administration constituted a major advance in the Federal Government's public
expenditure management. The new framework, founded on a transparent and objectives-based
programmatic structure, was expected to induce gradual changes in federal public administration
that would promote more performance-based management. This would be achieved by: (i)
clarifying program objectives and performance indicators; (ii) intensively monitoring the
implementation of pre-selected strategic programs; and (iii) launching an annual, comprehensive
program evaluation process. The Secretariat of Planning and Strategic Investment (SPI) within
the Ministry of Planning (MPOG) has led the PPA development and implementation processes.
106.  The Government has since conducted two annual PPA evaluations, presented the formal
reports to Congress and posted them on the MPOG website. While the quality of the evaluation
improved notably by the second year, and its results are reportedly used in the annual PPA
revisions, the SPI is conscious of the need to further improve the evaluation methodologies and
encourage more systematic use of evaluation results for resource allocation and program
management decisions. The new administration is currently preparing the next PPA for 2004-
2007 with a strong emphasis on the participatory process foi its elaboration.
29 The extension in 1997 was granted under the rubric of the Fundo de Estabilizacao Fiscal.
31



3. SIIAIF 21st Century Project
107.  The previous administration launched a project (SIAFI 21St Century) to renew the
existing financial management information system (SIAFI), which was originally developed in
1987. SIAFI has enabled reliable and timely monitoring and operations of public financial
management, but its technological platform has grown obsolete over time. The need for the
upgrading has been accentuated by the recent changes in Brazil's public finance regime due to
the LRF, the new PPA, and related innovations.
108.  The implementation of the SIAFI 21st Century Project has been delayed. Besides the
ambitiousness of the initial project implementation plan, project implementation was also
delayed due to a change of project managers and temporary cuts in the project's capital budget.
In view of the implementation delay, the Government developed two new components: (i) the
Brazilian Payments System; and (ii) "Availability of Revenues from the Source," using the
existing SLAFI platform, since they need to be integrated into the existing system. Once the new
SIAFI 215' Century is ready, these will be linked to the new platform. The Government also
designed a virtual training center, which is already available on the STN website, to facilitate the
transition of operational staff to the new platform and interface. The internal administration
subsystem has yet to be implemented. The budget, financial and patrimonial subsystem has only
partially been concluded. The project implementation timetable has been re-scheduled, and the
project is unlikely to be completed before 2005. It should be noted, however, that the existing
system, though becoming obsolete vis-a-vis today's technological standard, is fully reliable in
allowing timely and accurate expenditure control, and as such, the delay in the SIAFI 215'
Century Project implementation does not create major problems for the Government's financial
accountability framework.
4. Administrative Reform
109.  Administrative reform is one of the important pending reform agenda from the previous
administration. After the I9th Constitutional Amendment opened up a more flexible public
sector personnel management regime, a pending action to regulate and operationalize
Administrative Reform is the passage of a bill for Complementary Law No.248-D/1998. This
law would regulate conditions and procedures for the dismissal of tenured civil servants in the
three spheres of government and three Government branches. It would also establish criteria for
evaluating the performance of civil servants and for their dismissal in the event that they do not
meet such criteria. The Law formed part of a broader reform agenda launched in the mid 1990s
under the Master Plan for the Reform of the State. However, the consideration of this bill has
stalled in Congress for lack of political consensus on some of the specific content.30  Some
governors, however, have advocated that administrative reform accompany the proposed social
security reform.
30 Ninety one amendments have been introduced to this bill since 1998, diluting the original content of the bill to
such an extent that the Executive chose not to press for its passage. Its last debate took place in March 2002, when
three new amendment proposals were added by the Senate, but the bill has not been approved.
32



D.     SOCIAL SECURITY REFORM
a. Background and Issues
110.  Among the items that contribute to the excessive level of budget rigidity are the
entitlement programs that are designated as obligatory expenditures (and thus not subject to
expenditure cuts or control during fiscal adjustment). These expenditures are often indexed to
the minimum wage and thus tend to grow in correspondence to either the population growth or
increases in the minimum wage (so-called vegetative growth).3' Of these entitlement programs,
social security expenditures comprise the single most serious fiscal issue facing Brazil today.
Social security expenditures already pose heavy burdens on the government budget both at the
federal and sub-national levels. Brazil spent more than 11% of GDP on social security benefits
in 2001 and registered a cash deficit of 5.2% of GDP. This deficit is projected to grow, possibly
doubling in 30 years.
111.  Particularly problematic is the current regime for retired public sector employees (Regime
32
Pr6prio de Previdencia Social, or RPPS).  In terms of distributive impact, the current system
provides exceptionally generous benefits to retired public sector employees, particularly at the
federal level, who are relatively well-off and many of whom never made social security
contributions while actively employed. In 2001, the RPPS had about 3 million each of
contributors and beneficiaries and consumed the equivalent of 4.7% of GDP in benefit payments.
This contrasts with the private sector regime (RGPS) with about 30 million contributors vs. 18
million beneficiaries, and 6.3% of GDP in benefit payments in 2001. In terms of financial
sustainability, the RPPS accounts for the bulk of the social security deficit at 4.1% of GDP in
2001, in contrast to the RGPS deficit of 1.1% of GDP.33 It is clear from these figures that the
RPPS consumes a disproportionate share of public resources financed by general revenues,
which means that a relatively well-off minority of retired public sector employees is receiving
net transfers of resources from the general public, who are on average worse off.
112.  The current RPPS system also poses a serious threat to one of the most important
achievements in Brazil's fiscal management in recent years - continued compliance with the
Law of Fiscal Responsibility (LRF). Since social security benefit payments to retired public
sector employees are considered part of the personnel expenditure subject to the 60%/net current
revenue ceiling set in the LRF, the so-called vegetative growth of this expenditure item will
eventually make many sub-national governments unable to comply with one of the key
provisions of the Law, without adequate reform.
31 "Public Finance in Brazil: Policy Issues and Projections," by Raul Velloso, a background paper for the Brazil
Stabilityfor Growth and Poverty Reduction, Report No. 25278-BR, January 2003.
32 The Bank's analyses of these and other issues related to Brazil's social security system are found in Brazil -
Critical Issues in Social Security (Report No 19641-BR, June 2000)
33 It should be noted that an important source of the RGPS deficit is the inclusion of the rural pension program,
which many experts agree should really be considered a social assistance program to be financed from general
revenues rather than a funded social insurance program.
33



b. Government Actions: Achievements and Challenges
113.  These are well-known problems, and structural reform of the social security system has
long been recognized as a priority challenge in Brazil. The previous government began to
address this problem with the 20th Constitutional Amendment.  Although this amendment
introduced important reforms to the RPPS, it was primarily focused on reforms to the public
pension system for workers in the private sector. The amendment tightened some of the
eligibility criteria for public sector workers, (i.e., requiring 10 years of service, with 5 years in
the position from which the employee is retiring; a minimum retirement age of 60 for men and
55 for women; and a years-of-contribution criterion of 35 for men and 30 for women). The new
criteria also apply to existing staff (though the minimum retirement age is lower, at 53 for men
and 48 for women). In addition, the federal government and most states have instituted
mandatory employee retirement contributions. Federal employees must now contribute 11
percent of their pay to the federal public employee pension system. A number of state
governments followed suit.   Although  some states have tried to impose. retirement
"contributions" on existing retirees, thereby reducing net benefits, the Supreme Court has ruled
this unconstitutional.34
114.  While these earlier measures will help, they will not be sufficient. The costs of financing
the generous RPPS benefits based on a 100% replacement rate for the growing population of
eligible retirees from the public sector will require a level of employee contributions that is
politically implausible or a level of government contributions that is fiscally unsustainable.
Brazil can ill-afford the regressive distributive impact of the current RPPS system.
115.  Additional reforms are clearly needed. During the 2002 presidential campaign, President
Lula (then as a candidate) clearly signaled his intention to place a top priority on social security
reform. Upon assuming power in January, the Government initiated an active process of broad
consultations to develop consensus for a government proposal. The president created the
Council for Economic and Social Development as a new institutional mechanism for
consultation and advice, and placed social security reform as the first item for its consideration.
Following this broad consultation process, the Government submitted on April 30 a proposal for
a constitutional amendment to reform the social security system for the public sector employees.
The proposal, if approved intact, will still not fully resolve all the weaknesses of the current
system. However, it is a very ambitious proposal, especially given the entrenched opposition
that has successfully deterred major reform attempts in the past. The main elements of the
reform proposal are the following:
/ Doubling the minimum period of affiliation and increasing the retirement ages;35
V  Charging current retirees a contribution of I 1% of benefits above R$1,058;
Benefit ceiling for new retirees at R$2,400, the same amount for the new benefit ceiling
for the private sector regime; retirees would have the option of complementing this
benefit with a complementary pension fund, but no retiree would be able to receive a
pension benefit higher than R$12,720;
34 The Bank supported these reform measures with a series of two sector adjustment loans in 1999-2000.
35 The current requirements are 10 years of service, 5 years in the position from which the employee is retiring. The
current retirement ages are 48 years for women and 53 years for men. The proposal would raise them to 55 and 60
years for women and men, respectively
34



/ Calculation of the public sector retiree benefits on the basis of their net average salary for
the reference period; those who have worked in the private sector would have the benefits
rules in the private sector regime applied in proportion to the time spent in private sector
employment instead of having automatic access to the full-salary pension scheme in the
public sector as is the case now; and
v Reduction of the benefit calculation ratio for the survivor pension program from 100% to
70% of the reference salary.
IV. PROPOSED SECOND PROGRAMMATIC FISCAL REFORM LOAN
116.  The proposed Second Programmatic Fiscal Reform Loan is based on three sets of
justifications.
(a)   First, there has been good progress in important institutional and structural reforms,
as set out in the First Programmatic Fiscal Reform Structural Adjustment Loan
(PFRSAL), although progress in different technical areas has not been uniform. The
most noteworthy achievement is the progress toward institutionalizing responsible fiscal
management. The initiation of key structural reforms such as tax reform also merits
Bank support within a medium-term programmatic framework. The Bank will continue
its policy dialogue and technical assistance in policy areas in which progress has been
more limited. A later section discusses in detail progress achieved since the first
PFRSAL.
(b)   Second, and beyond the specific measures taken and supported by this loan, the
responsible policy stance taken by the new Government more broadly provides a very
favorable context for the proposed operation. This favorable context includes, inter alia,
progress in social security reform, responsible monetary policies, as well as decisive
policies to address poverty and inequality directly. This context is even more important
as it shows that a broad consensus on the basic elements of sound econormic and social
policies has evolved. This will facilitate implementation of consistent policies in the
medium and long term.
(c)   Third, despite the positive recent developments, Brazil still finds itself in a fragile
position vis-a-vis international financial markets. There are clear signs that market
confidence has substantially improved since the beginning of the year when President
Lula began his four-year term, which is evidenced in the recent successful international
bond issuance, for the first time since April 2002. Nonetheless, access to international
markets is still precarious. Bank financial assistance in support of fiscal reform would
send a positive signal to the market of the Government's efforts and achievements so far
and could accelerate Brazil's transition toward regaining full market access to meet its
external financing needs and strengthening its net reserves.
35



A.    PROGRAMMATIC FRAMEWORK, LOAN DESIGN, AND POSSIBLE FUTURE LOANS
a. Programmatic Framework
117.  The proposed loan forms part of the programrmatic framework that encompasses an
ambitious reform agenda, addressing three broad objectives of fiscal reform in Brazil: (i)
institutionalization of responsible fiscal policy and risk management; (ii) improvements in
efficiency and equity in the revenue structure; and (iii) efficient and equitable public
expenditures geared toward provision of public goods for poverty reduction and growth
promotion (the first two objectives are the focus of the proposed loan). To achieve each of these
objectives, a set of relevant policy areas and specific policy actions have been identified as
comprising the overall fiscal reform program (see Annex 2). However, given the ambitious and
wide-ranging nature of the reforms, it would be unrealistic to expect simultaneous progress in all
areas within the programmatic framework. The Bank would, thus support subsets of this reform
agenda as the Government progresses in one or more of these areas. Each individual loan within
the programmatic framework would be based on the completion of a critical mass of actions
within a subset of the areas covered, as illustrated in the Figure 4 below. Specific loans will be
discussed in more detail below.

118. This framework subsumes and expands on the technical areas covered in the first
PFRSAL, namely, (i) macro fiscal management; (ii) public expenditure management, and (iii)
public debt management. The expansion of the programmatic framework has its origin in the
arrival of the new government with a new and broadened agenda of fiscal reform, which required
us to revisit the scope of the overall program as well as relative priorities among its various
elements. For example, while reaffirming its strong commitment to continue with the
responsible fiscal management as a key policy priority, the new Government has also indicated
its intention to highlight the importance of the quality of public spending overall and its impact
on poverty reduction. The Bank has initiated more involved dialogue with the authorities on
these latter issues, including a proposal to conduct public expenditure reviews and program
impact evaluations with Bank assistance. As the Government's medium-term program in these
areas develop further, the Bank intends to incorporate them more fully into the programmatic
framework and support them with future operations.
b. Status of the First Programmatic Fiscal Reform SAL Benchmarks
119.   As reported in the Implementation Completion Report on the first PFRSAL, overall
outcomes of the set of policies the loan supported were satisfactory, even though some of the
expected benchmark actions were not completed. The status of the PFRSAL benchmark actions
is summarized in Table 10 and is discussed further in this section.
120. Progress in macro-fiscal planning/management, sub-national fiscal discipline, and aspects
of public debt management has been notable. As regards macro fiscal planning/management, the
first Loan envisaged as benchmark actions the meeting of the Government's fiscal targets (e.g.,
primary surplus, debt/GDP ratio), improvements in fiscal reporting and transparency (e.g.,
consolidation of public sector accounts, and consolidation and analysis of sub-national LDOs to
assess the entire public sector's fiscal prospects and risks), and enforcement of the LRF and the
state debt refinancing agreements. As detailed below, the Government met most of these
benchmark actions, especially the crucial ones: it surpassed its own primary surplus targets in
both 2001 and 2002, and obtained approval of two Senate Resolutions to regulate sub-national
indebtedness according to the requirement of the Law of Fiscal Responsibility (LRF). Good
fiscal performance is clearly demonstrated in the sub-national governments' strong record of
compliance with the LRF.
121.  Although some capacity building measures in public debt management were delayed
somewhat, the overall progress in this component was judged satisfactory. The benchmark
actions expected in the first Loan included issuance of the STN debt managers' code of conduct,
upgrade of the Middle Office's analytical capacity, and issuance of annual borrowing plans to
guide the STN operations in debt management. The Government completed these actions,
especially in strengthening the Middle Office's analytical capacity. The STN made partial
progress toward meeting other benchmarks.  For example, the STN has completed the
consolidation of domestic debt issuance responsibilities. However, the Government postponed
the earlier decision to transfer external debt management responsibilities from the Central Bank
for fear of exacerbating the market uncertainty in the midst of the volatile external environment
Brazil faced over the last two years.
37



122.  Progress was relatively slower in the public expenditure management component of the
Loan, which supported (i) the introduction of a new multi-annual plan (PPA) for 2000-2003 with
innovative results-oriented framework, (ii) the SIAFI21st Century Project to upgrade the federal
integrated financial management system; and (iii) administrative reform.
123.  In the PPA component, the first Loan envisaged development of formal program
monitoring and evaluation system; better integration of planning and evaluation with budgeting
as evidenced in adjustments to budgetary priorities on the basis of the evaluation results; and
establishment of the PPA Management Information System (SIG) with public access via internet.
The Government registered concrete progress in initiating a systematic annual PPA evaluation
process, and submitted to Congress evaluation reports in two consecutive years (2001 and 2002).
There is room for improving the evaluation methodology used, and with Bank technical
assistance, the Ministry of Planning has been exploring measures to strengthen the
methodological and procedural aspects of the PPA evaluation framework.
124.  Slippage was most significant in implementation of the SIAFI 215' Century Project, a
project to upgrade a well-functioning but increasingly obsolete integrated financial management
system to a new technological platform. The delay in project implementation was due to a
combination of the originally over-ambitious implementation plan and some budgetary
restrictions. The adequate functionality of the existing system means that the delay in the project
implementation has so far not caused major disruptions to the quality of federal financial
management.
125.  Finally, approval of the Complementary Law bill to regulate the 19'h Constitutional
Amendment on Adrninistrative Reform, which would have permitted more flexible,
performance-oriented personnel management, has been pending in Congress due to political
opposition.
126. The relatively slower progress on the last-mentioned components of the PFRSAL is
unfortunate but has not compromised the overall progress toward consolidation of fiscal reforms
in Brazil. Because of the relatively slow progress in the public expenditure management
component overall (in spite of reasonable progress in some aspects of the PPA sub-component)
but its continuing importance, it was decided that the Bank would continue policy dialogue in
this area with relevant authorities and would retain this area within the programmatic framework
but would not include this component in the proposed PFRL 2. The amount of the proposed loan
is smaller than it would have been if there had been equivalent progress in the public expenditure
management area.
38

c. Loan Design
127. The proposed loan would support a series of actions already taken by the Government to
advance the two broad objectives identified above. Specifically, the loan components include:
(i) macro-fiscal planning, (ii) effective control of sub-national debt and deepening of sub-
national fiscal discipline; (iii) improvements in fiscal transparency/reporting and management of
contingent liabilities; (iv) capacity building and strengthening of internal governance
arrangements for public debt management; (v) development of secondary markets for
government securities; and (vi) initiation of a tax reform to reduce the tax system's distortionary
and regressive effects on the national economy.
Institutionalization of responsible and crediblefiscal policy and fiscal risk management
o   Strengthening of macro-fiscal planning: The overall objective is to reduce volatility and
uncertainty arising from fiscal policy decisions in a volatile external environment. Over the
past several years, the Government has been developing a credible medium-term fiscal
framework. Credibility has been enhanced by the achievements of the announced primary
surplus targets in four consecutive years. The Government is attempting to institutionalize
this credibility by improving the quality of its medium-term fiscal projection and planning,
primarily through the LDO Annex on Fiscal Targets. The proposed loan would support (i)
the achievements of the primary surplus targets in 2001-02, and (ii) adoption of annual
primary surplus targets of 4.25 of GDP for 2003-2006 in the 2004 LDO bill. These targets
40



are higher than the target agreed with the IMF in the ongoing program, which shows the
Government's commitment to prudent fiscal policies.
* Effective control of sub-national debts and sub-national fiscal discipline: The overall
objective is to maintain the fiscal effort undertaken by sub-national governments and to
promote more broad-based compliance with the LRF and associated legal norms. The
proposed loan would support (i) the passage of the Senate Resolutions 40 and 43 to regulate
sub-national\,indebtedness as required by the LRF, (ii) the National Monetary Council
Resolutions 2827 and 2920 to regulate the financial sector's credit supply to the public
sector, as well as (iii) the impressive turnaround in sub-national fiscal behavior as evidenced
in the effective compliance with key provisions of the LRF - the personnel expenditure/net
current revenue (RCL) ratio below 60% and the debt stock/RCL of 2.0 or less for states and
1.2 or less for municipalities. The resolutions have created a robust regulatory environment
to minimize the risk of excessive sub-national borrowing in the future, while the actual
performance by the majority of the sub-national governments shows that these legal
provisions have been effectively complied with.
* Improvements in fiscal transparency and reporting: The overall objective is to build on
the already solid government efforts to improve fiscal transparency as a versatile measure to
encourage fiscal discipline and public sector accountability. Even before the LRF (which
places a strong emphasis on fiscal transparency and reporting), Brazil had adequate fiscal
transparency based on the comprehensive financial management system (SIAFI) and other
instruments. Since the LRF's approval, however, Brazil has made additional progress in this
area, with most of the federal units providing regular fiscal reports.
The government's ex post recognition of contingent liabilities (or "skeletons") has
contributed to the 25% increase of federal debt between 1994 and 2001. To minimize
unrecognized growth of contingent liabilities in the future, and as required by the LRF, the
Government formally adopted a transparent method of discussing fiscal risks in an LDO
Annex. The Annex identifies multiple sources of fiscal risks and assesses sensitivities of the
budget and the public debt to different scenarios. With this new practice, the Government
achieved substantial transparency, a necessary first step for effective management of
contingent fiscal risks.
The proposed loan would support (i) the issuance since 2001 of consolidated public sector
accounts from the Union, all the state governments, and the vast majority of the municipal
governments; (ii) incorporation of a substantial amount of previously unrecognized liabilities
("skeletons") into official debt figures; (iii) official reporting of contingent liabilities in the
LDO Annex on Fiscal Risks; and (iv) the initiation of fiscal statistics reporting based on the
IMF SDSS methodology.
* Capacity building and strengthening of the internal governance arrangements for
public debt management:     Substantial progress was achieved in the institutional
development of the middle office and the Annual Borrowing Plans. The STN has already
adopted its own code of conduct in line with international best practice. The overall
objective of this set of measures is to create the governance structure necessary to implement
the benchmark developed by the middle office of the STN's Debt Management Office. It is
important that the STN centralize debt management (domestic and external) functions, to
make debt managers accountable for public debt risk levels. The centralization of the
41



domestic debt management functions has already been achieved. This would also be a
necessary step to meet the parallel objective of establishing an autonomous central bank,
accountable for monetary and exchange rate policy. The performance indicator of
achievements of this objective would be meeting the targets set in the Annual Borrowing
Plans during the 2003-2006 period. By meeting the targets, exposure to rollover, exchange
rate, and interest rate risks will be diminished. The governance structure described in the
Debt Management annex should also be established.
The proposed loan would support concrete achievements so far in terms of: (i) issuance of
Annual Borrowing Plans; (ii) consolidation of domestic debt issuance responsibilities under
the STN; (iii) the strengthening of the analytical capacity of the Middle Office as evidenced
in regular reporting of good quality debt management reports; and (iv) completion of an
exercise to map STN processes to control operational risks in debt management.
o   Market development for government securities: The -overall objective here would be to
develop a domestic market for different types of securities, to permit the implementation of
the associated benchmark (i.e., possibility of issuing long term securities, fixed rate nominal
debt, etc.). The proposed loan would support (i) initiation of the retail sales of public bonds
through the internet ("Treasury Direct"), (ii) issuance of regulations concerning new criteria
for the selection of primary dealers and specialists, (iii) improvements in methods for
issuance of government securities, (iv) transfer of regulation and supervision of collective
investment schemes in fixed income securities, and (v) establishment of formalized
cooperation between the Central Bank and CVM in market regulation.
Improvements in efficiency and equity in the revenue structure
o   Initiation of tax reform: The loan would support recent advances in tax policy changes,
including (i) the transformation of the turnover tax PIS/PASEP into a value-added tax (Law
10.637), and (ii) the submission of a tax reform bill (PEC 41/03) to Congress after broad
consultations. The main content of the tax reform proposal includes unification of the ICMS
state VAT tax rates, conversion of the COFINS tax base from turnover to value-added, and
flexibility in setting the CPMF tax rate between 0.38% and 0.08%.

d. Possible Future Loans
128.   Over the next four years, several (3-5) additional loans within this programmatic
framework could be proposed if and when a critical mass of positive reform actions or
institutional improvements is obtained (see Figure 1). This section discusses possible clusters of
such reform actions as bases for future loans to demonstrate how the programmatic framework
would translate into concrete operations. Annex 2 summarizes the program content and future
44



development actions. The triggers shown in Annex 2 and discussed below would be the core
actions supported by future loans. A critical mass of additional development actions from Annex
2 would be required to move ahead with each loan. In addition, the decision on whether to move
ahead with the next loan would be informed by an assessment whether Brazil is on track toward
the outcome indicators listed for 2006, which is the end of the program period.
(a)   A follow-up operation to support further institutionalization of fiscal responsibility and
completion of the tax reformn: There are further significant steps ahead to consolidate the
institutionalization of responsible fiscal management in Brazil. A big, positive step
would be the formal adoption of an explicit fiscal rule, or an equivalent institutional
framework, to guide setting of key fiscal targets. Strengthening of the institutional
underpinnings of responsible fiscal policy would be complemented by continued
improvements in public debt management governance and capacities. The Ministry of
Finance might consider further strengthening the Debt Management Committee and
creating a Council for Public Debt Management with an explicit accountability
arrangement. Implementation of the postponed decision to transfer external debt
management responsibilities from the Central Bank to the STN would constitute another
positive step in strengthening governance of public debt management. These actions
would constitute triggers in the debt management governance area. In the area of
government debt market development, the triggers would be the following CVM actions:
(i) establishment of a uniform regulatory framework for collective investment schemes;
and (ii) issuance of regulation to strengthen the protection of investors trading
government and other securities through brokers on an exchange.
This possible loan could be triggered by Congressional approval of the pending Senate
resolution to control federal indebtedness, and of complementary/ordinary laws to
regulate specific details of the reform proposals after the passage of the Constitutional
Amendment Proposal (PEC) 41/03. The amendment and the complementary laws will:
(i) establish a unified legal framework for the ICMS state VATs; (ii) clarify the collection
principle (origin-based vs. destination-based); and (iii) set the rate for the CPMF tax
(financial transaction tax) between 0.38% to 0.08%. By then, the conversion of COFINS
from a turnover-based to a value-added-based tax will be well on its way. The approval
of these complementary laws is expected within the next 18 months or so. Triggers in
the debt management include (i) completion of the transfer of external debt management
responsibilities from the Central Bank to the STN.
(b)   An operation to support improvements in public expenditure efficiency: Improving the
quality of public expenditures is one of the oft-mentioned goals of this Government. To
this end, the Government is currently working on a new multi-year investment plan
(PPA) for 2004-07. It is expected that many of the innovative features introduced in the
previous PPA, which PFRSAL supported, would be kept; while other features, such as
broader consultations in the plan preparation, would be added. The PPA proposal will be
submitted to Congress by August 2003, and will later be discussed and approved.
Another important measure already proposed by the Government is the extension of the
federal revenue de-earmarking arrangement (DRU), which is due to expire at the end of
2003. The legislative approval of the DRU extension and adoption of innovative features
45



in the next PPA, including enhanced prioritization of government objectives, could be
triggers for a possible public expenditure loan to support advances in related areas such
as better integration of planning and budgeting, program evaluations, development of a
medium-term expenditure framework, and implementation of the SIAFI 215' Century
Project.
To improve efficiency and targeting of its public expenditure programs, the Government
is considering adoption of annual public expenditure review exercises as part of its
annual budget process. At the initial stage, the Bank would work together with the
Government to develop capacity for robust expenditure reviews and assist in their
institutionalization over time.
(c)   An operation to support consolidation of public expenditure reform: Within the four-
year period, the Government could make important progress toward consolidating the
reform of the federal public expenditure system.  Beyond extension of the DRU
arrangement, the Government could attempt legal or constitutional reforms to mitigate
negative effects of some of the revenue earmarking arrangements that may no longer be
justified from the points of view of the Government's policy priority and expenditure
efficiency. Institutional development in the area of public expenditure management
(PEM) could advance further with institutionalization of robust program evaluations and
expenditure reviews as integral parts of the medium-term planning and budgeting
process. Other improvements in PEM could be codified in a new public finance
complementary law, as mandated by the Constitution, which would serve as a trigger.
Approval of this complementary law could serve as a trigger for a possible follow-up
loan in PEM, but this would be a medium-term agenda, for which technical preparation
and political consensus-building would be necessary. Thus, this measure will likely be
taken over the medium term (i.e., 3-4 years from now). Another possible trigger is
congressional approval of the pending Complementary Law bill 248-D/98, or equivalent,
to the define public sector career structure and other features of performance-oriented
federal personnel management.
(d)   If the Government achieves significant progress in other areas within or related to the
fiscal reform program, this could be supported either within the above mentioned or
additional separate operations.
129.  Continued implementation of a sound macroeconomic program, of which the proposed
policies and reforms are part but which extends beyond that, is a precondition for continued
lending under this programmatic framework. A disbursing program with the IMF would be
evidence of such satisfactory program.
130.  The total amount of financing that could be made available to Brazil over the next four
years through further loans within this programmnatic framework will depend on the lending
envelope to be determined in the forthcoming CAS. However, given the importance of the
structural reforms to be supported by the proposed programmatic framework, such financing for
additional loans could conceivably reach or even exceed US$2.0 billion.
46
