B.      COUNTRY CONTEXT AND TIMING OF BANK FINANCIAL ASSISTANCE
132.   Besides the progress in the technical areas described above, there is important contextual
rationale for proceeding with the proposed loan at this point. As described in the following
paragraphs, these contextual factors are no less important for the Bank to consider timely support
for Brazil. The favorable country context described immediately below provides the Bank with a
degree of confidence that the supported reform measures will have a reasonable prospect for
success and sustainability, while the particular timing of the proposed operation could be
especially valuable for Brazil to accelerate its transition toward renewed external market access.
a. Favorable Count,y Contextfor Structural Reforms
133.   President Lula's administration arrived in the midst of heightened market uncertainty.
The market was concerned about Brazil's external financing requirements, high domestic debt
and interest rates, and inflationary pressures. In response to the market expectations, the new
48



Government has demonstrated its commitment to sound macroeconomic management through
the reassuring inaugural speeches given in January 2003 by the newly appointed economic team.
These speeches were quickly followed up with decisive measures that sent strong signals of
fiscal responsibility. First, the government announced in early February a new primary surplus
target of 4.25% of GDP. This is well above the level previously agreed in the IMF Agreement,
and higher than any previous primary surplus achievement. Second, to make this primary
surplus target viable, the Government announced drastic cuts in spending limits authorized in the
annual budget, while largely protecting social expenditures. Third, by withholding part of the
constitutional transfers to some large states for their failures to comply with certain LRF
provisions, the Government also signaled that it will enforce the fiscal obligations of states and
municipalities within the framework of the Law of Fiscal Responsibility and the State Debt
Refinancing agreements, a key issue in the sustainability of public finances in Brazil.
134. As for much-needed structural reforms, the Government announced plans to rapidly
pursue key reforms in. the areas of the pension system for public sector . employees, the
complicated tax structure, and the establishment of Central Bank autonomy. A proposal for a
Constitutional Amendment, which is a necessary condition for proceeding with the latter,
recently obtained support of an overwhelming majority (442 votes out of the total 513, as
opposed to 308 votes (60%) required for passage of a constitutional amendment) in the first
round of voting in the Lower House.36 This marked an important show of political force behind
the Government's reform program and signaled the transition from the initial phase of
Government announcements to a new phase of implementation of key reforms.
135.  The tax and social security reform proposals have been developed through broad
consultation and consensus building by the Council for Economic and Social Development, a
newly established independent organ created to deliberate on priority issues and advise the
President on policy options. In parallel, the Government has promoted and conducted broad
consultations in seminars and meetings with organized groups representing different societal
interests as well as key political actors such as governors and mayors. One tangible result of
these efforts is the so-called Letter from Brasilia signed and published in late February following
a successful consultation with the governors of all 27 states. The letter (attached as an annex)
laid out in very concrete terms agreed directions for the two key reforms, and the Government
subsequently presented to Congress to Constitutional Amendment proposals based on these prior
consultations. As detailed in the relevant annexes, the technical content of the reform proposals
consistent with what most experts have long advocated.
b. Contribution of Bank Financial Assistance at a Critical Juncture
136.  The Bank's financial assistance would help Brazil meet its external financing
requirements, which in 2003 are estimated at some US$35 billion. This estimate is based on a
US$7 billion current account deficit and on US$28 billion amortization of medium and long-
term debt (excluding IMF). The role of foreign direct investment in bridging this gap is reflected
in the forecasted flows for 2003 of US$16 billion, compared to flows of US$23 billion for 2001.
36 Senate approval is pending.
49



137.  Apart from financing balance of payments needs, the Loan would help meet the federal
government's external financing requirements of about US$9 billion in 2003 and help lengthen
the term structure of public sector debts and thus reduce vulnerability. With improved market
sentiments vis-a-vis Brazil, sovereign bond spreads have dropped below 800bps as of April
2003. Nevertheless, in the context of international economic uncertainties and the perception of
emerging market country risk, access to commercial external debt financing for Brazil remains
precarious and, if available, the cost of alternative internal and external debt financing extremely
high. Unlike IMF financial support, the loan would contribute to Net International Reserves, and
as such is expected to help further increase market confidence and thus accelerate the return to
sustained market access.
C.    DESCRIPTION OF FiNANCIAL ASSISTANCE AND CONDITIONS FOR DISBURSEMENT
138.  The Bank's financial assistance under the PFRL II would comprise a loan of US$404.04
million to be disbursed in a single tranche after loan effectiveness. With this loan, Bank lending
for Brazil in the extended CAS period FYOO-03 would remain well within the overall lending
ceiling for the base case. However, the loan would marginally exceed the notional amount for
adjustment lending indicated in the CAS within the overall CAS envelope. Bank exposure
would remain lower than if the full CAS envelope had been committed in the extended CAS
period. Going beyond the indicated amount for adjustment lending is justified based on the
resolution of uncertainty that prevailed last year about Brazil's economic policies after the
elections, the excellent performance of the new administration, and the persisting difficulties in
accessing international financial markets.
D.    COUNTRY ASSISTANCE STRATEGY UPDATE
139.  The Bank's approach toward the new administration is driven by the desire to help Brazil
capture the opportunities to achieve lasting and rapid social progress while reducing
macroeconomic risks. Through strong engagement of the new government team before it took
office, through a range of instruments including the policy notes and the visits of Mr.
Wolfensohn in November 2002 and March 2003, the Bank has quickly established close and
constructive working relationships with the new administration. The opportunities and risks of
the current situation and the excellent positioning of the Bank justify a high level of Bank
engagement and support to the new Government.
140.  In this context, the Bank is preparing a series of policy-based lending operations
(programmatic loans) in areas ranging from human development (approved in February 2003),
fiscal reform (this proposed operation), reforms to improve competitiveness and the investment
climate, and financial sector reforms (the latter following two Programmatic Financial Sector
Reform Loans in recent years). These operations would complement the ongoing US$30 billion
IMF standby arrangement and support the Government's reforms for advancing social progress,
assuring economic and fiscal stability, and fostering growth. These operations would play a key
role to: (a) continue and deepen key economic and sectoral reforms; (b) finance part of the
nominal fiscal deficit and the external financing requirements of the public sector; and (c)
reinforce the markets' perception of the commitment of the new administration to sound
economic and sectoral policies. The timing of this operation is meant to send a strong and
visible signal of support during this crucial early period of the new Government.
50



141.  Building on the Policy Notes and policy discussions with the new Government, the Bank
is currently preparing the new Country Assistance Strategy (CAS) for Brazil. The new CAS will
focus on the five themes of the Policy Notes: investing in people, growing through productivity,
stabilizing the economy, delivering services to all, and managing Brazil's natural environment.
The CAS will also emphasize the up-scaling of successful poverty reduction approaches and the
critical role of knowledge in Brazil's development.  The four-year program of the new
Government (Plano Plurianual - PPA) will be an essential input and will drive the timing of
CAS finalization. Board presentation of the CAS is foreseen for early FY04.
E.    LINK WITH OTHER BANK SUPPORT
142.  The operations most directly relevant to the proposed loan are the Fiscal and
Administrative Reform Loan (FARL, 2000) and the Programmatic Fiscal Reform SAL (2001).
The former supported the Government's Fiscal Stability Program, fiscal reform at the state level
(the, State Debt Refinancing Law, the State Debt Refinancing Agreements, and the new Sub-
national public indebtedness regime), and administrative reform. The FARL's overall impact
was rated satisfactory in the ICR. Later, the Bank adopted an explicit programmatic framework
with the PFRSAL so as to support the Government's medium-term reform agenda in a more
explicit fashion, and prepared a TAL (Fiscal and Financial Management TAL, or Proger) to
support implementation of the agreed benchmark actions. The ICR rated the PFRSAL to be
satisfactory overall.37
143.  Proger has been a main vehicle with which the Bank has assisted the Government's
capacity building agenda especially in public debt management and training of municipal
governments in fiscal management in compliance with the LRF requirements. Proger is also
supporting capacity building in the Ministry of Planning in the area of planning and program
evaluation, a theme expected to be supported by one or more of the future programmatic loans as
illustrated above. The Bank could accommodate the Government's possible new demands for
technical assistance, especially in areas that we expect to support with future programmatic
loans. Possible areas for new technical assistance within the programmatic framework include
capacity building of the Federal Budget Secretariat in budget management and budget process
reform, development of a secondary market for government securities, among other possibilities.
144.  Together with other recent or possible future fast-disbursing loans, the proposed loan
forms a consistent and coherent program to support the new Government's policy agenda for
poverty reduction, growth and stability. The debt management and debt market development
component of this loan is closely linked with the overall capital market development strategy
supported by the financial sector reform loans. A possible future loan for competitiveness would
complement financial sector reforms in a comprehensive approach for a productivity-focused
growth agenda. The recent Human Development Programmatic Sector Reform loan supports
policies critical for poverty reduction and complements and deepens in the social sectors the
expenditure reform program outlined in this document.
37 The ICR rated the outcome as "satisfactory," sustainability as "likely," and institutional development impact as
"substantial
51



145. The recently completed Country Assistance Evaluation (CAE) concluded that the Bank
support for Brazil's fiscal reform agenda over the last few years had been "relevant and
effective." The CAE also noted as a priority "continued support for fiscal adjustment and
reform, possibly in the form of additional programmatic adjustment lending, conditional on the
generation of substantial primary fiscal surpluses and a reduction of public sector debt, the
deepening of the administrative reforms, and the implementation of the long-delayed tax
reform." The Bank's medium-term strategy for supporting Brazil's fiscal and public sector
reforms will be articulated in the next CAS that will be prepared in coming months. While
continuing lending assistance (both fast disbursing and technical assistance) with the
programmatic framework as proposed in this document, the Bank is in the process of developing
programmatic AAA to intensify policy dialogue on fiscal and public expenditure management
issues.
F.    LINK WITH OTHER PARTNER PROGRAMS
146.  The programmatic framework for Bank support links closely with support from the IMF
and the IDB. The supported program is fully consistent and mutually reinforcing with the policy
framework supported by the ongoing IMF stand-by agreement. The proposed loan supports
reforms that deepen the overall framework underlying the IMF program in several areas where
the Bank has actively collaborated with the Government, in particular public debt management
and fiscal risk management. Similarly, work for future phases of the programmatic framework
in public expenditure management and social security reform, complements and deepens the
policy framework underlying the IMF Program.
147.  In September, 2002, Brazil and the IMF agreed on a program with two main objectives:
first, to establish a clear policy framework for the medium term; and second, to facilitate an
orderly transition to the new administration taking office in January, 2003. The four pillars of
the program were: (i) maintenance of a primary fiscal surplus of 4 percent until June 2003; (ii)
commitment to a primary surplus of 3.75 percent of GDP for 2003-2005; (iii) continued
implementation of the inflation targeting framework in the context of a floating exchange rate
system: (iv) continued progress in structural reforms. The March 2003 review of the program
concluded that all performance criteria were met, though inflation exceeded the upper limit of
the program's consultation band. This was attributed to the unexpected depreciation of the
currency, of more than 50 percent, during 2002. The review also added as structural benchmarks
for reform, the tax reform and the social security reform, which are object of support of this
program. Other structural benchmarks included in the IMF program are the de-earmarking of
revenue and the reduction of the CPMF, discussed throughout this document. Hence the
proposed PFRSAL addresses the main structural reform benchmarks incorporated in the IMF
agreement, thereby making it perfectly complementary with the IMF financing package.
148.  IDB finances two large projects to support fiscal and tax administration at the sub-
national level.38 These are aimed at strengthening sub-national capacity and complement World
Bank support under the programmatic framework.
38 These projects are. the National Fiscal Administration Program for the Brazilian States (1996) and the National
Program to Support the Administrative and Fiscal Management of Brazilian Municipalities (1999).
52



G.    PROGRAM IMPLEMENTATION AND SUPERVISION
149.  Regular Bank missions will review progress in the implementation of the proposed
reform program and their outcomes. Reviews will involve Bank technical teams working in
collaboration with the Ministries of Finance and Planning, and the Central Bank, in accordance
with the responsibilities of each agency described in Annex 2. The reviews will assess
compliance with conditionalities and with the fiduciary responsibilities of the Borrower. Bank
reviews will also consider the effective implementation of social programs that have been
protected under this loan.
H.    COMPLIANCE WITH BANK POLICIES
150.  The Loan complies with all applicable Bank policies.
1.    DISBURSEMENTS, AUDITING AND FIDUCIARY ENVIRONMENT
151.  The Loan would disburse under the Bank's provision for fast disbursing operations.
Disbursement will be the result of the compliance of conditionality for PEFL 2 presented in
Annex 2. The flow of funds would follow procedures now well established under prior
programmatic adjustment loans.
* The Bank deposits the proceeds in a Government's account at Banco do Brasil, New York;
* The proceeds enter into the Central Bank of Brazil's International Reserve Account,
denominated in dollars;
* The Central Bank enters the counterpart proceeds, denominated in domestic currency, into
the Government's account at the Central Bank (the Conta Unica do Tesouro). This account
earns the average yield of Treasury bills at the Central Bank;
* The Conta Unica do Tesouro has a classification of the funds by revenue source. The
domestic currency proceeds at the Government's account at the Central Bank are classified as
Resources from Foreign Credit (account item no. 148).
152.  The Bank may require audits of the account into which the proceeds of the loan will be
disbursed.
153.  As discussed in more detail in the 2002 CAS Progress Report, Brazil has a supportive
fiduciary environment for the proposed operation. Furthermore, the Government is engaged in a
process of strengthening it expenditure review, financial management, and auditing functions.
The Bank has been supporting several related initiatives.
* The Federal Government has consolidated effective and transparent expenditure planning,
budgeting, and financial management systems over the last years. These systems include
multi annual planning (Plano Plurianual - PPA), strategic budget planning, the annual law of
budget guidelines, and the budget law itself. The monitoring and evaluation system of the
PPA constitutes a framework for gradually institutionalizing public expenditure review that
are built into the regular planning and budgeting cycle.
53



o The Bank, in coordination with the Brazilian Govermment, has concluded the Country
Financial Accountability Assessment (CFAA) that reviews the systems and procedures used
by the GoB at the national level to budget, expend, account for, report on, and audit the use
of funds approved in the annual budget. This review concludes that the Brazilian system of
public financial management provides reliable information. Adequate systems exist to
manage and track the receipt and use of funds at the national level an there is a high level of
fiscal transparency, both of which would support any program of adjustment lending. The
risk to both Bank and country funds is low.
o  In specific areas, the Bank also supports borrowers in their procurement systems. Regarding
Bank-financed projects in general, the Brasilia-based implementation team continues to
support and underpin high standards with respect to financial management, procurement, and
accountability.
J.    ENVIRONMENTAL ISSUES
154.  The proposed loan focuses on economic management issues and is classified as a SAL
without an environmental impact category. However, the broader programmatic framework
includes policy areas, such as public expenditure management, which have important
environmental linkages.  An environmental analysis of several areas covered by the
programmatic framework was therefore carried out. The main findings are that, during the fiscal
adjustment, aggregate expenditures on environmental programs apparently did not change much,
although there was significant reallocation across programs and areas, and from the Environment
Ministry to other government bodies. This - as well as some restructuring of MMA - appears to
reflect an emphasis that government bodies other than MMA should play a larger role in the
protection of the environment, since policies in many sectors have environmental impacts. The
reallocation of environmental expenditure allocations across ministries was facilitated by the
new and flexible budgeting system introduced by the government since 2000, which emphasized
the cross-cutting roles played by different government ministries. Nevertheless, the reallocation
of funds has caused a number of programs to be cut, and it is possible that the funding for more
of these programs could have been maintained without fiscal adjustment. However, cuts in
discretionary spending, including some environmental expenditures, were also a necessity of the
fiscal adjustment supported by this loan. They are a product of the structural constraint of the
Brazilian budget characterized by the excessive level of statutory rigidity and the government's
announced commitment to protect social expenditures from budget cuts.
K.    RISKS
155.  One risk of the proposed operation is that the legislation submitted to Congress, in
particular tax reform legislation, would not be approved. While this risk exists, it should be
recognized that, unlike attempts by the previous Government to introduce tax reform legislation
to Congress, the current process of consensus building on social security and tax reforms,
involving agreements with State Governors and within the new Council for Economic and Social
Development, reduces the risk substantially and makes timely approval of reforms very likely.
Also, the recent approval of the Amendment to Constitutional Article 192 demonstrates the
political support the Government currently commands in Congress.  Based on these
54



considerations, as well as the importance of the proposed reforms, and the overall progress of the
Government program, this risk is considered acceptable.
156.   A second risk is that new negative shocks could undermine debt sustainability. If in such
a downside scenario, Brazil failed to increase the primary surplus suitably, the perception that the
debt may not be sustainable would result in higher spreads and make the situation worse. To
incorporate uncertainty into the debt sustainability exercise, stress tests of the debt dynamics
were performed. The object of the stress testing exercise is to see how the net public debt path
changes when extreme, but possible, events shock the system (see Annex on Fiscal
Sustainability).
157.   The stress scenario is built upon the 10 percent confidence level shocks for most
variables.39 Under such a bleak scenario (which, with ninety percent probability, would not
materialize), the exchange rate would depreciate and lead to higher inflation, under the
assumption of a 40 percent pass-through in the following year.40 The variables were shocked in
2003 and returned to their steady state level through time: It was assumed that growth would
stabilize at about 2 percent per year, and spreads would decrease given that the debt is
permanently increasing. The real interest rate is assumed to remain at 12 percent throughout the
simulation period, and the real exchange rate is assumed to remain constant after the shock.4' In
this scenario, a 4.25 percent of GDP primary surplus would not be enough to stabilize the
debt/GDP ratio, which would increase somewhat over the next few years without further action
(see Annex on Fiscal Sustainability). Even in this bleak scenario, the worsening debt-to-GDP
ratio trend could be arrested, through decisive action by the government - for example, through
the attainment of an even higher primary surplus.
158.   Since 1999, Brazil has built a track record of quick fiscal policy responses to negative
shocks. The Government's commitment to adjusting the fiscal stance to changing circumstances
in order to stabilize the debt ratio is credible. Thus, even if the bleak scenario described in the
previous paragraph were to materialize, the country's previous track record indicates that further
adjustments would be undertaken by the government in order to control the situation. The current
fiscal stance represents a careful balance between the need for a sufficient safety margin to
accommodate negative shocks and signal to markets fiscal credibility with the need to maintain
effective public services and meet the social ambitions of the new Government, considering that
structural reforms to increase budget flexibility are aggressively pursued but will take time for
implementation.    Under these circumstances, the remaining        fiscal risks are considered
acceptable.
39 See Brazil CEM 2003 for further technical details. As a reference point, consider that financial institutions realize
the stress testing exercises with a .01 or .025 confidence level. This implies that the confidence level we are using is
not imposing extremely demanding requirements. These scenarios that consider jointly the changes in all the
variables, with changes derived from individual empirical distributions for each of the variables may be
overestimating the true likelihood of all the events happening simultaneously. However, the fact that our model
does not allow for repeated shocks in the future (since shocks in the model are uncorrelated over time) tends to
underestimate the likelihood of having a growing debt ratio in the future
40 This coefficient is in the lower bound of the estimates presented in Tables 6 and 7 of Goldfajn and Werlang
(2001); see Annex 4 which is on fiscal sustainability.
41 This assumption implies that the shocks to the real exchange rate are permanent or that are very slow to reverse.
This assumption is based on the non-rejection of the unit root hypothesis of the series, as discussed below.
Alternative exercises reported below relax this assumption.
55



159.  A final risk arises from the possibility that the central bank cannot lower interest rates
due to persistent inflationary pressures. With real interest rates in the double-digit levels, growth
will be subdued and unemployment could keep rising. Under these circumstances political
pressure could mount to change the economic strategy. In particular the discussion of Central
Bank autonomy would be difficult. Given the decisions adopted until now, it is unlikely that the
new administration will succumb to pressures to change the economic policy course, and this
risk is considered acceptable. Most importantly, the reforms supported by this loan and the
financial support provided by the loan are expected to reduce the risks discussed in this section.
56



ANNEX 1: LETTER OF DEVELOPMENT POLICY
Brasilia, May 2003
Mr. James D. Wolfensohn
President
The World Bank
Washington, DC
Dear Mr. Wolfensohn:
1.    This letter of sector policy discusses progress in the economic stability program of the
Brazilian Government, especially the developments in its fiscal and debt management policy
framework. We are writing to request financial assistance from IBRD, in the form of a
programmatic adjustment loan, in support of the implementation of these policies. Brazil's Fiscal
and Federal Debt Management Reforms are central components of the Government's structural
reform program. We believe they constitute important initiatives of the Brazilian Government to
be supported by the Bank under a programmatic adjustment loan.
Macroeconomic Outlook
2.    The Brazilian economy went through intense volatility last year, especially in the second
half, as a result of the heightened risk aversion external scenario as well as of the uncertainties,
from the market perspective, regarding the Brazilian macroeconomic conditions. Such factors
were also reflected in the domestic financial market, which posed significant challenges to the
management of the public debt, and resulted in a sharp decrease in the availability of foreign
finance. The exchange rate faced heavy pressure throughout the year, resulting in a depreciation
of the real, in relation to the US dollar, of around 50%. Also, one of the most well-known
indicators of risk in the financial market almost tripled, reaching around 2,400 base points in
September last year. Although the economy successfully weathered these shocks, as reflected in
a sharp swing in the Current Account, the depreciation of the real contributed to an acceleration
of inflation which reached, as measured by the Consumer Price Index (IPCA), 12.5% per year.
The fight against inflation has, thus, been a lynchpin of the economic policy in 2003, which is
aimed at reducing inflation to the medium-term targets established by the Government.
3.    In the fiscal area, the new Government promptly announced an increase in the target for
the non-financial public sector primary surplus to 4.25% of the GDP, 0.5 percentage point above
the previous target. The strengthened fiscal effort is being made mainly through a substantial cut
in expenditures, in contrast with the adjustment made during 1999-2002, which was in large part
based on new taxes or hikes on existing taxes. The Budget Guidelines Law (Lei de Diretrizes
Or,amentarias - LDO), submitted to Congress in April 2003, strengthened the fiscal framework,
by setting the primary target for 2004-2006 at 4.25% of GDP, the same as for this year. The need
for achieving these targets is easily understood when consideration is given to the value of the
public debt in relation to GDP. The Government understands that the current high levels of this
ratio is an impediment to sustainable growth and an important constraint on the pursuit of social
policies aimed at reducing the income disparities that for far too long have marked Brazilian
57



society. The maintenance of a surplus of 4.25% of GDP will be vital for achieving a reduction in
the debt-to-GDP ratio to about 50% in 2006, permitting an important drop vis-a-vis the peak of
63% reached in the second half of 2002.
4.    Aiming at reverting the inflationary expectations, Banco Central do Brasil adopted a
restrictive monetary policy, increasing the yearly basic interest rate by 8.5 percentage points, to
26.5%, as well as increasing the reserve requirements on cash deposits starting from the third
quarter of 2002. On the other hand, in the face of last year's exceptionally adverse external
scenario, the inflation targets for 2003 and 2004 were increased to 8.5% and 5.5%, respectively.
The previous targets were 4% and 3.75%, with a 2.5-point tolerance margin above and below.
The objective of such an adjustment is to allow the convergence of inflation to the medium term
targets in the longer term.
5.    The exchange rate devaluation and the consequent adjustment of relative prices had a
noteworthy positive .impact in the balance of payments. The current accQunt deficit sharply
decreased from 4.5% of the GDP in 2001 to 1.7% in 2002, mainly as a result of the commercial
surplus, which increased to US$ 13.1 billion. For 2003, conservative official projections estimate
a surplus of US$ 16 billion, which would result in a current account deficit of 1% of the GDP. It
is noteworthy that such an important external adjustment was achieved contemporaneously to
GDP growth, reflecting a swing in external accounts resulting chiefly from changes in relative
prices rather than a compression of domestic demand. Real GDP growth in Brazil was 1.5% in
2002, with growth in 2003 projected at around 2%. With the consistency of the fiscal and
monetary policies, the adjustment in the balance of payments and the major reforms announced
by the Government, the risk perception of foreign and domestic investors fell substantially,
falling below 800 basis points. The reduction in the risk perception fostered the resumption of
foreign financing and an appreciation of the exchange rate of about 17% since the end of last
year. The inflation rate, although still high, is clearly on a downward trend. The projection of the
IPCA inflation for April is 1%, compared to 3% in November last year.
6.    The performance of the main economic indicators in the first months of this year
indicates that the Government has adopted adequate policies. The Government is also strongly
committed to a broad reform agenda, including changes in taxes, social security and capital
markets, with a view to ensure the resumption of sustainable and balanced economic growth with
more equitable social impacts. The tax reform presented to Congress, further detailed below as
part of the proposed operation, aims chiefly at improving the efficiency of the Brazilian tax
system, while promoting economic growth and job creation, and reducing inequality. To ensure
the sustainability of public finances, while improving equity in public spending, the Government
is committed to reducing the structural imbalance of the social security system for public
servants. Currently, this imbalance is of the order of 4 percent of GDP. To address this issue, a
Draft Constitutional Amendment was submitted to Congress at end-April. This Draft
Constitutional Amendment comprises, among others, proposals to double the minimum period of
affiliation entitling public servants to a pension, and to change the basis for calculating
retirement benefits from the last salary to the net average salary; it also envisages reducing the
benefit of future survivor pensions from 100 of percent to 70 percent of the reference salary.
Once approved, the social security reform will bring long-lasting benefits to the public accounts,
while providing more equity between public and private pensions. The financial market reforms
envisaged by the Government, an important element for a solid financial intermediation,
58



comprises the proposal to Congress of a Draft Bankruptcy Law, measures to enhance the
autonomy of Banco Central do Brasil, as well as a set of regulatory measures aiming at
improving credit guarantees and the functioning of lending markets.
7.    Given the hard fiscal constraints to be faced in the next years, improving the quality of
public expenditures, particularly in terms of their efficiency and targeting, has become a key
challenge and priority of the Brazilian Government. Regarding efficiency, new methods of
results-oriented management by programs are gradually spreading throughout the federal public
administration, and coordination and cooperation have improved among the key central agencies
involved in public expenditure management. The Government also recognizes that improvement
in targeting social expenditures to achieve greater social impact is an important challenge to be
tackled over the medium term. The new Pluriannual Plan - PPA for 2004-2007, now being
prepared, will constitute the guide for Brazil's public expenditure programs over the next four
years. The Plan would signal the Government's strategic priorities, to be embedded within a
consistent macroeconomic and fiscal framework, as well as in annual budgets.  The
institutionalization of the annual PPA evaluation is viewed as an important step towards
improving the quality of decision-making on public policy and expenditure choices, as well as a
better integration of the planning, budgeting and management of federal programs. The
Government is also looking into developing an institutionalized process of regular public
spending reviews as an integral part of the annual budget decision-making process. An
important medium-term agenda is to analyze options to reduce budgetary rigidities related to
expenditures and revenues. In this regard, the Government is proposing to extend the
Desvincula!do de Receitas da Uniao (DRU) and intends to explore other measures over the
medium term.
Fiscal and Federal Debt Management Reforms
8.    The Brazilian Government is fully committed to the sustainability of public finances, in
order to provide a macroeconomic environment conducive to growth and the reduction of
poverty and inequality. This is the overall objective of its fiscal policies and of the reforms that
are being openly discussed with Congress and the society. One of the main objectives of
Brazil's fiscal policy is to make public finances, and hence the economy, more resilient to
shocks. To do so, the Government's strategy is to further advance in developing institutions to
ensure a better quality of fiscal adjustment. Brazil has taken major strides already. Particularly
noteworthy is the adoption of, and consistent compliance with, the Fiscal Responsibility Law
(LRF) which, among other benefits, has helped to keep public debt growth in check and to create
a new culture of accountability among those responsible for public spending. In our determined
adherence to the principles of fiscal responsibility in addition to other important reforms referred
to above, it is our intention to further strengthen the advances in the debt management and
taxation areas, mainly along three dimensions: (i) reducing uncertainty regarding fiscal policy
decision-making; (ii) reforming the tax system; and (iii) reducing the risk profile of public debt.
i) Reducing Uncertainty in Fiscal Policy Decision-Making Process
9.    To minimize uncertainty arising from the fiscal policy decision-making process, we
intend to continue clarifying fiscal policy objectives and the instruments and indicators to
monitor progress toward the objectives. This approach is already embedded in the recent
submission to Congress of the draft law of budget guidelines (Lei de Diretrizes Orqamentarias
59



2004). Our aim is to ensure that public policy is not a contributing factor to accentuate output
fluctuations, but a means to guarantee access of the public sector to adequate financing
resources, under all circumstances, in order to allow the Government to perform its essential
activities without inefficient disruptions. In this context, it is our intention to guide fiscal policy
with the long-run objective of ensuring sustainability of the public debt.
10.   To guarantee debt sustainability, the Government has adopted an intermediate objective
of reducing the net public debt to around 50 percent of GDP by 2006. A strong primary fiscal
surplus will be the main policy tool towards achieving this end. With the announced targets of
4.25 percent of GDP for the primary surplus, we believe that the intermediate objective regarding
the debt ratio can be achieved in the next three years. However, if unforeseen circumstances lead
to deviations from the trajectory towards this objective, we would take measures to stay on
course.
11.   In order to ensure the meeting of such a debt to GDP ratio, and to set and implement new
and lower debt targets, the Government intends to continue studying, in the design of its fiscal
policy, rules that combines the long tern objective of public debt sustainability with the short
term objective of reducing pro-cyclical bias in fiscal policy. Additionally, the Government
intends to continue strengthening the institutional framework for ensuring prudent fiscal policies.
12.   Responsible fiscal management has permeated all levels of government in Brazil. At the
level of the 27 States (including the Federal District), only eight of them ran primary surpluses in
1998, but that number had risen to 21 by 2001. Our objective is to continue promoting
institutional strengthening and maintenance of fiscal responsibility at the State level, which
should lead to a greater number of States generating primary surpluses. Similarly, the current
average ratio of net debt to net revenue for States is already at 1.6, much lower than the ceiling
of 2 established though Senate Resolution 43. We believe conditions are favorable for this ratio
to stabilize or show a small decline in coming years.
ii) Reforming the Tax System
13.   To ensure sustainability of public finances, in addition to the reforms in the capital
markets and social security areas referred to above, the Government's strategy in the near-term is
to focus on reducing the burden of an overly complex tax system and the risks of damaging tax
competition among States and the Federal District. Accordingly, following an unprecedented
meeting with the States and Federal District Governors and broad consultation with society, a
Draft Law was submitted to Congress setting the backbone of a tax reform. The proposed Law,
would convert turnover taxes (such as PIS/PASEP and COFINS) into value added taxes, unify
ICMS tax legislation and rates across states, make room for substituting payroll taxes with a
value added tax, and set the path for the gradual reduction of the debit tax (CPMF) rate; these
will have an important impact on economic efficiency in the next few years.
iii) Reducing the Risk Profile of Public Debt and Fostering Development of Markets
for Government Securities.
Governance of Debt Management Process
14.   The Government intends to continue conducting its debt management within a
framework that grants an important role to diminishing risks, in addition to cost considerations. It
60



also intends to continue strengthening the governance arrangements and high standards of
transparency and accountability that have steered the decision making process in this area.
15.   The overall objective of the Government's debt management is to reduce over time the
exposure to rollover, interest rate and exchange rate risks, while ensuring-under a prudent
standard-the lowest financing costs to the Treasury. The current agenda for Government debt
management-which is underpinned by the envisioned maintenance of a strong and permanent
primary fiscal surplus-includes a number of actions with respect to organizational and
governance arrangements, as well as debt management strategy.
16.   Regarding the organizational and governance arrangements, we intend to formalize over
the next few years the organization and functions of the Debt Management Committee within the
Secretaria do Tesouro Nacional (STN). In addition, the establishment of a Public Debt Council
(PDC) is being considered. Among the functions for the PDC under consideration would be the
approval of the Govemment's debt management strategy and the associated Annual Borrowing
Plans. These new governance arrangements-and the transparency and accountability standards
they entail-will further enhance the existing process of formulation, approval, monitoring, and
evaluation of the Government's debt management strategy. Also, as envisioned under the Fiscal
Responsibility Law, the issuance and management of the Government's external debt, which at
present are handled by Banco Central do Brasil, should be moved to and consolidated at the
Secretaria do Tesouro Nacional. Improvements on the techniques used to set and implement the
strategy for managing the public debt will continue to be pursued, including those regarding how
best to incorporate the different risk dimensions influencing the annual borrowing plans.
Fostering Development of the Market for Government Debt
17.   Efforts to strengthen the governance and strategy for debt management have to be
complemented by a structured and well-sequenced approach to the development of the local
government debt markets. To this end, our action plan focuses on three key and complementary
strategic dimensions: (i) designing and implementing a more explicit short- and medium-term
domestic debt issuance strategy (necessary to enhance transparency and predictability); (ii)
broadening of the institutional and retail investor base and increasing its diversity (necessary to
enhance demand in the primary market); and (iii) fostering greater liquidity in local secondary
markets for government debt.
18.   As regards the development of a more explicit and predictable debt issuance program, as
outlined in our Annual Borrowing program and mentioned earlier, the Government is setting
target ranges consistent with reducing the proportion of dollar-linked and SELIC-indexed debt
issued. To reinforce this, the Front Office of the Debt Management Office is beginning to
develop a detailed short-term and medium-term domestic debt issuance program, consistent with
the debt management objectives. That should lead to the gradual establishment of more liquid
benchmarks and an associated yield curve. In particular, the Government is interested in
developing a program for the regular issuance of Treasury Bills (LTNs), without losing sight of
the end of the yield curve.
19.   The Government is also focusing increased attention on improving the structure and
resilience of the end-investor base. This effort would be necessary to enhance the market for
61



government securities. This strategy would also increase the ability of institutional investors to
more effectively disclose and manage risks.
20.   The Brazilian Government plans to address theses issue in several ways. Regulatory
oversight by Comissao de Valores Mobiliarios CVM (the Brazilian securities commission) will
be increasingly important. In line with this objective, the Government has developed a
Memorandum of Understanding between CVM and Banco Central do Brasil, designed to permit
explicit resource sharing. Going forward, the Government is considering the establishment of an
inter-agency team to assist CVM in developing a new regulatory framework for equity and fixed-
income funds (including hedge funds).
21.   The Government is also considering options to broaden the investor base and increase
competition for savings products by further developing the Treasury Direct, a system that allows
retail investors to buy Government securities over the internet. To this end, the Government is
exploring ways to allow a broader group of institutions to distribute Government securities
through linkages to the Treasury Direct system. To further support liquidity, to increase
competition, and improve the price-finding process of public debt, the Government is
considering the introduction, in the near term, of a new two-tiered primary dealer system
(specialists and primary dealers).
Request for Financial Assistance
22.   The Government remains firnly committed to its program of reforms as outlined above
and would welcome World Bank financial assistance. We appreciate the prompt consideration of
the second programmatic adjustment loan in the fiscal and debt management sectors, in support
of the measures that have already been enacted and are under implementation. We look forward
to working together with the Bank on other proposed future loans as further progress in these
areas takes place.
Yours sincerely,
Antonio Palocci
Minister of Finance*

Reforrnas Fiscal e do Gerenclamento da Divida Federal
8.     0 Govemo brasileiro tem fimme compromisso com a sustentabilidade das finan9as
publicas, de maneira a oferecer um ambiente macroecon8mico que promova a crescimento e a
redu,co da pobreza e da desigualdade. Esse 6 o objetivo maior das suas politicas fiscais e das
reformas que estao sendo discutidas com o Congresso e com a sociedade de forma aberta. Um
dos principals objetivos das poifticas fiscals brasileiras e torner as finean,as pubicas, e
consequentemente a economia, mais resistente acs choques. Para esse fim, a estratbgia do
Govemo e avan,ar ainda mals no desenvolvimento das Instituic,es para assegurar um aluste fiscal
de melhor qualidade. 0 Brashi ja conqulstou avanQos importantes. Merece particular registro a
ado,co e o cumprimento consistente da Lot de Responsabilidade Fiscal (LRF) o que, entre outros
beneffcios, ajudou a manter controle sobre a divida publEca e criou uma nova cullura de

determinada aos prtnclpios da responsabilidade fiscal e adlcionalmente As Importantes refomras
referides acimna, 6 nossa lntencao aprofundar ainda mais os avan,os nas Areas de gerenclamento
da divida e trlbutacao, principalmente em trAs .dimensoes: (1) redu,co da Incerteza relativa ao
processo decis6rio da politica fiscal; (ii) reforma do sistema trlbutaino; e (Iii) redugao do perfil de
risco da divida publica.
(ij Redu;io da Incerteza no Processo Decls6rlo da Politica Fiscal
9.     Para minimizar as Incertezas decorrentes do processo decls6rlo da polftlca flscal,
pretendemos continuar a esclarecer os objetivos da politica fiscal e os Instrumentos e indicadores
para monitorar o progresso rumo aos objetivos. Essa perspectiva ja estA Incorporada na recente
proposiXo ao Congresso do Projeto de Lei de Diretrizes Orcamentarias 2004. Nosso objetivo 6
assegurar que as politicas p6iblicas nao sao um fator que contribua para acentuar flutua0oes dos
resultados, mas um melo para garantir o acesso do setor p(ublico a recursos financeiros
adequados, em todas as circunstAnclas, de forma a permltr ao Govemo desempenhar suas
atividades essencials sem interrupK6es ineficlentes. Nesse contexto, A nossa Inten,Ao orientar a
politico fiscal para o objetivo de longo prazo de assegurar a sustentabilidade da divida puiblica.



10.    Para garantir a sustentabilidade da dIvids, o Govemo adotou o objetivo intermediario de
reduzir a divida publica liquida para aproximadamente 50% do PIB ate 2006. Um forte superavit
prmaro fiscal sera a principal ferramenta de politica voltada para atingir esse fim. Com as metas
anunciadas de 4,25% do PIB para o superavit primario, acreditamos que o objetivo intermediario
relaUivo A relag,o dfvida/PIB pode ser alcangado nos pr6ximos tres anos. Entretanto, se
circunstanclas inesperadas levarem a desvios nessa trajet6ria, medidas de corre,co serAo
tomadas.
II.    De maneira a assegurar que essa relac3o divida/PIB seja atingida e que novas metas
ainda menores seJam implementadas, o Govemo pretende continuar a estudar, no desenho de
suas polfticas fiscais, regras que combinem o objetivo de longo prazo de sustentabilidade da divida
publica com a meta de curto prazo de reduzir a influencia prociclica na polftica fiscal.
Adicionalmente, o Govemo pretende continuar a reforcar a estrutura institucional encarregada de
assegurar politicas fiscais prudentes.
12.    0 gerenciamento fiscal responsavel permeou todos as esferas de govemo no Brasil. No
nivel dos 27 Estados (incluindo o Distrito Federal), apenas oito deles realizaram superAvit primrnio
emr 1998, tendo esse numero se elevado para 21 em 2001. Nosso objetivo e continuar a promover
o reforco institucional e a manutencao da responsabilidade fiscal no nivel estadual, o que levari a
um maior numero de Estados a gerar superavites primarios. Similamnente, a atual media da
relacao divida liq0ida/receita liquida para os Estados ja esta em 1,6, muito abaixo do teto de 2
estabelecido pela Resolu,ao do Senado no. 43. Acreditamos que as condic6es sao favoraveis para
que essa relacao se estabilize ou mostre algum declinlo nos pr6ximos anos.
ii) Reforma do Sistema Taibutrio
13.    Para encorajar a sustentabilidade das financas p6blicas, adicionalmente As reformas nas
Areas de mercado de capitais e previdencia mencionadas acima, a estrategia do govemo no curto
prazo esta focada em reduzir o fardo de um sistema tributario extremamente complexo e os riscos
de competig6es tributarias danosas entre os Estados e o Distrito Federal. Nesse sentido, seguindo
a uma reuniio sem precedentes com os Govemadores dos Estados e do Distrito Federal e
consultas A sociedade, um Projeto de Lel foi submetido ao Congresso estabelecendo a espinha
dorsal de uma reforma tributaria. A proposta Lei, convertendo Impostos sobre o faturamento (como
o PIS/PASEP e o COFINS) em impostos sobre o valor agregado; unificando a legislacao e as
aliquotas do ICMS para todos os Estados (incluindo o DF); abrindo a possibilidade de substituir
impostos sobre a folha de pagamentos por impostos sobre o valor agregado; e estabelecendo o
caminho para a gradual redugao da aliquota da CPMF, terA um importante impacto na eficiencia da
economia nos pr6ximos anos.
iii) Reduzindo o Perril de Risco da Divida Publica a bncentivando o Desenvolvimento
dos Mercados para os Titulos do Govemo
Governanga do processo de gerenciamento da divida
14.   0 Govemo pretende continuar a conduzir o gerenciamento da sua divida em um contexto
que incorpore explicitamente considerac6es sobre risco em adigAo a custo. Ele tambem continuara
a reforcar os arranjos de govemanra e altos padr6es de transparencia e de atribuicao de
responsabilidade que tem orientado o processo decis6rio nessa Area.
15.    0 objetivo geral do gerenciamento da divida do Govemo e reduzir progressivamente a
exposiQao aos riscos de rolagem, de taxas de juros e de taxas de cambio, ao mesmo tempo em
que assegura - seguindo padr6es prudentes - o mais baixo custo de financiamento ao Tesouro. A
atual agenda para o gerenciamento da divida do Govemo - que e apolada pela esperada
'.  d



manulencao de um forte e permanente superavit primario fiscal - inclui um conjunto de a,6es
relativas aos arranjos organizacional e de govemanca, bem como A estrat6gia de gerenciamento
da divida.
16.   Relativamente aos arranjos organizacionais e de govemanca, pretendemos formalizar nos
pr6ximos anos a organiza,co e func6es do ComReA de Gerenciamento da Divida, no Ambito da
Secretaria do Tesouro Nacional. Adiclonalmente, o estabelecimento de um Conselho da DIvida
PGblica (CDP) estA sendo considerado, Entre as func6es do CDP que estio sendo consideradas
estaria a aprovacao da estrategia do Govemo para a divida publica e os relacionados pianos
anuals de financlamento. Esses novos arranjos de govemanca - e os padr6es de transparencia e
atribuicAo de responsabilidade que eles imp6oem - aperfeicoarao ainda mais o atual processo de
formula,co, aprovacao, mon-toramento e avaliacao da estrategla do Govemo para o
gerenciamento da divida. Adicionalmente, conforrne previsto na Lei de Responsabilidade Fiscal, a
emissAo e gerencia da divida extema do Govemo, que presentemente e feita pelo Banco Central
do Brasil. devera ser consolidada e transferida A Secretaria do Tesouro Nacional.
Aperfeigoamenlos nas tecnicas usadas para definir e implementar a esirategia para o
gerenciamento da divida publica deverao continuar a ser buscados. inclusive com relacao A melhor
forma de incorporar as diferentes dimensoes de risco que influenciam os planos anuais de
financdamento.
Incentivando o Desenvolvimento do Mercado para ritulos do Govemo
17.    Esfor,os para aperfeipoar a govemanga e a estrategla para o gerenciamento da divida
devem ser complementados pelo desenvolvimento estruturado e bem seqaenciado dos mercados
para a divida dos govemos locals. Com essa finalidade, nosso piano de acao define tres
dimens6es estrategicas principais e complementares: (1) desenho e implementacAo de uma
estrategia de emissAo de divida de curto e medio prazos (necessarla para aumentar a
transparencia e previsibilidade); (ii) ampliacao da base de Investidores institucionais e de varejo e
aumento da sua diversidade (necessario para ampliar a demanda no mercado primario); e (ii)
incentivo A maior liquidez nos mercados secundarlos locais para dividas do Govemo.
18.   Relativamente ao desenvolvimento de um programa de emissao de divida mais explicito e
previsivel, conforme esbo,ado em nosso programa anual de financiamento e mencionado
anteriormente, o Govemo estA estabelecendo metas consistentes com a reduq,o da proporcAo de
emiss6es de divida indexadas ao d6lar e indexadas A SELIC. Para reforgar, o Front Office da
unidade de gerenciamento da divida esta iniciando o desenvolvimento de um detalhado programa
de emiss8es domesticas de divida de curto e medio prazo, consistente com os objetivos de
gerenciamento da divida. A implementacAo desse programa de emissao deveria levar ao
estabelecimento gradual de indicadores de malor liquidez - e uma curva de rentabilidade
associada. Particularmente, o Govemo esta interessado em desenvolver um programa para a
emlssAo regular de Titulos do Tesouro (LTNs), sem perder de vista a construcao de uma curva de
rentabilidade.
19.   0 Govemo esta tambem focalizando crescente atencao em melhorar a estrutura e
elasticidade da base de investUdores finais. Este esforco sera necessario para fortalecer o mercado
de Titulos do Govemo. Essa estrategia tambem ampliaria a capacidade dos investidores
institucionais de informar e gerenciar rsco.
20.    0 Govemo brasileiro planeja enfrentar essas quest6oes de diversas maneiras. A supervisAo
regulat6ria pela Comissao de Valores Mobiliarios - CVM sera crescentemente importante. Em linha
com esse objetivo, o Govemo desenvolveu um Memorando de Entendimentos entre a CVM e o
Banco Central do Brasil desenhado para permitir explicito intercAmblo de informa,ao. Mais alem, o
Govemo esta considerando o estabelecimento de uma equipe inter-agencias para assessorar r
I 



CVM no desenvolvimento de uma nova estrutura regulamentar para fundos de a,6es e de renda-
fixa (incluindo fundos de hedge).
21.    0 Govemo tambem estA considerando altemativas para ampliar a base de Investidores e
aumentar a concorrnncia par instrumentos de poupan,a pelo desenvolvimento adicional do
Tesouro Direto, um sistema que permite investidores no varejo comprar Titulos do Govemo pela
intemet. Com essa finalidade, o Govemo estA planejando explorar meios de permitir a um grupo
mais amplo de institul6es distribuir os Titulos do Governo por intemmedio de ligag6es com o
sistema do Tesouro Direto. Para dar ainda mais liquidez, aumentar a competl,io e melhorar o
processo de defini,co de pre,o da divida p6blica, o Govemo esta considerando a introdu,co, em
breve, de um novo sistema de distibuldores primarios em duas faixas (distribuidores especialistas
e primarios).
SolicitagAo de Assistrncia Financeira
22.    0 Govemo permanece firmiemente comprometido com seu programa de refornas
dellneado acima e apreciaria a assistencla financeira do Banco Mundial. Agradecemos a pronta
consideracao do segundo emprestimo programntico nos setores fiscal e de gerenciamento da
divida, em apoio As medidas que ja foram adotadas e As que estgo sendo implementadas.
Contamos com a oportunidade de trabalhar conjuntamente com o Banco em futuros emprestimos
conforme os progressos em outras Areas forem verificados.
Atenclosamento
ntonio Palocci

ANNEX 3: BRASILIA LETTER
In a meeting in Brasilia on February 21-22, 2003, the President, accompanied by the Vice
President, Ministers, Congressional leaders, and the 27 State Governors concurred that reforms
of the pension and tax systems were priorities in order to generate sustainable economic growth.
Thus, they signed an agreement to submit these reforms in the first semester of 2003 to
Congress, a sovereign forum for taking decisions in these areas. Aware that the debate on such
reforms should also immediately involve the society as a whole, they have decided to announce
publicly the following points of agreement reached during their meeting:
A. On tax reform
1. The new tax system shall promote fiscal fairness and increase the efficiency and
competitiveness of the economy, though the exoneration of taxes on exports and the  -
stimulation of production and investment. It will also be necessary to streamline the existing
tax system and fight fraud and tax evasion.
2. The reform shall be revenue neutral for all members of the federation and, without
increasing the overall tax burden, it should aim to broaden the tax base and improve tax
administration, to generate conditions to reduce the tax burden on the most fragile sectors of
the economy.
3. The Constitution shall define the new local value-added tax (ICMS) as a unified state tax
in the country, with identical legislation and standards, in order to reduce the number of tax
rates and eliminate the 27 different legislations overseeing this tax which exist today. The
transition rules will be defined in a Federal law, passed with a qualified majority.
4. The employer's contribution to finance social security will be levied, totally or partly, on
turnover rather than on payroll, reducing the burden on employees' wage bill and with a
view to promote the formalization of employment. This contribution will be exclusively
earmarked to finance the social security system. The transition to this new system could be
gradual.
5. The gradual reduction in the incidence of cascading social taxes shall be promoted based
on the experience with the PIS, with a view to reducing the distortionary effect of the tax
system on the economy. This reform shall also preserve the efficiency of the tax collection,
thus requiring that the transition be pursed carefully.
6. The reform shall increase the progressivity of the tax system and promote the fairness of
the tax system, though a reduction of the tax burden on basic goods, and revision of direct
taxes.
7. All levels of government should participate in a tax education campaign to engage the
population in a common effort to fight tax evasion.
71



8. A sustainable regional development policy shall be defined to reduce regional inequalities,
in particular in the Northeast, North and Center-West regions, as well as in other less
developed regions, and resolve the existing tax war between States.
9. Municipalities shall be strengthened as the main units for the develop of social inclusion
policies and for the access to services essential to the population.
10. The final report of the Lower House's Special Commission for Tax Reform shall serve as
basis for the definition of a tax reform proposal, as it shall reflect the large amount of debate
that is taking place in Congress on the matter, in particular as regards the balanced
participation of the sub national and federal government in mechanisms to stimulate
production and exports.
B. On Social Security Reform
There was agreement on the following diagnostic:
1. The urgent need to reorganize social security to ensure that the rights of the actual and
future generations are protected, and to maintain the distributive and contributive aspects
of the systems.
2. The severity of the country's social security situation across regimes.
3. The highly redistributive role of the General Social Security Regime administered by the
Instituto Nacional de Seguridade Social (INSS), which covers more than 21 million
beneficiaries and pays the minimum wage in two thirds of all cases.
4. That the general regime is more than 80 percent auto-financed (97 percent when
considering benefits and contributions in urban areas).
5. That the special regimes for public servants presents a large financial imbalance at all
levels of sub national and Federal governments, putting at risk the financing of social
policies and public investment in the short, medium, and long run.
6. That the special regimes are only 50 percent auto-financed at the Federal and State
levels, as well as in the majority of municipalities.
7. That the trend is of a deterioration in this situation during the next 10 years if no new
measures is taken, and that, in various States, the situation is already critical.
8. That the main cause for the imbalance is the eligibility criterion, which is incompatible
with the nature, remuneration, and protection of the public servant carrier.
In view of this situation, it was decided to:
72



1. Reaffirm the respect of already-acquired rights for those already retired, as set in the law;
2. Preserve the thrust of existing rules, based on direct contributions , of the General Social
Security Regime administered by the INSS, given their redistributive nature and the good
prospects for self-sustainability of this regime; promote the fight against fraud and tax
evasion; and seek the inclusion of the new generations of Brazilians in this system.
3. Seek the recovery in the value of the ceiling of the General Regime, which has been
declining relative to the minimum wage, by linking it to GDP growth; also promote a
gradual rise in the floor for benefits, in line with efforts to preserve the real value of the
minimum wage.
With respect to the Special Regimes for public servants, it was decided to:
1. Jointly prepare proposals for constitutional reform of the Special Social Security
Regimes, to revert the existing actuarial and financial imbalance and, therefore, fulfill the
mandate of Article 40 of the Constitution.
2. Propose new rule for eligibility to these regimes, in particular with respect to retirement
age and minimum length of service in the job and in the public service, in addition to new
rules for survivor benefits.
3. Promote the necessary legal changes to enabie the contribution to current retirees and
establish a minimum contribution rate for all Special Regimes.
4. Support the approval of PL-9 by Congress, in order to establish the basis for the creation
of complementary pension funds for new entrants in the public service.
5. Support the approval of measures that make viable the constitutional ceiling on public
servants pay.
6. With a view to achieving the objectives above, prepare in the next 30 days studies at the
States' level to assess the impact of these reforms on the sustainability and redistributive
features of the regimes, to prepare the technical implementation of these reforms.
Brasilia, February 22, 2003.
73



ANNEX 4:     PUBLIC DEBT SUSTAINABffLITY IfN BRAZIL42
1.    The simple cross-country comparison depicted in Figure 1 suggests that Brazil's main
problem regarding public debt sustainability is its high real interest rate rather than the size of its
debt. Indeed, Brazil's public debt, at just over half of GDP, is not high in comparison with that
observed in various high-income countries-such as Italy, Belgium, Japan and Canada. Of
course, interest rates and public debt are related because the former-especially in the long
run-reflect fiscal sustainability considerations. (In practice, short-term interest rates are largely
determined by exchange rates and expectations regarding inflation, while longer-term rates are
highly dependent on expectations regarding public-sector solvency). Note that this cross-country
comparison does not take into account the many differences between Brazil and the other
countries analyzed; in particular, a country with developed domestic financial and capital
markets is likely to be better able to handle high debt levels than one where these markets are not
developed.

A. The Level of Brazilian Interest Rates
2.    The negative real interest rates that characterized the financial repression era of the 1960s
and 1970s are long gone. During the decade between 1975 and 1984, real interest rates on
deposits were, on average, negative because of unexpected changes in inflation, imperfect
42 This Annex is a summary of a longer and more detailed discussion found in Brazil. Stabilityfor Growth and
Poverty Reduction, Report 25278-BR, The World Bank, 2003.
74



indexation and other interventions designed to keep the rates low (or negative). After 1983, with
increasing financial liberalization, real interest rates on time deposits rose sharply, reaching 10
percent on average between 1985 and 1989. With inflation acceleration in the mid-1980s,
indexation intervals became shorter, and a share of deposits was held in accounts linked to the
daily behavior of overnight interest rates.
3.     Brazil's success in bringing down inflation with the Real Plan in mid-1994 was also
associated with real exchange rate appreciation. This upward trend in the real exchange rate
originated in the fiscal imbalances that were occurring at the time, coupled with the use of the
nominal exchange rate as a nominal anchor, which led to capital inflows. To avoid a monetary
expansion induced by capital flows, inflows were partly sterilized. Sterilization created
significant fiscal costs that raised public sector borrowing requirements, which in turn, put
upward pressure on pressed real interest rates.
.4.    These inconsistencies undermined      the credibility  of the economic program, and
international reserves were drained away in an episode that ended in the Real crisis of 1999. By
any standard, Brazil negotiated its way through this crisis with extraordinary ease and speed.
The main reasons for this quick recovery was a policy regime that combined three elements: (1)
the floating exchange rate system, (2) the inflation targeting system that provided a clear rule for
monetary management, and (3) a strict and austere fiscal policy that led very quickly to the
generation of public sector primary surpluses of over 3 percent of GDP. This consistent policy
framework brought down average interest rates over the 1999-2001 period. However, since late
2001, real interest rates have been on the rise, eventually hovering at around 10 to 13 percent in
real terms.
5.     Two factors determine the level of Brazilian interest rates: (1) monetary policy, and the
way it affects and reacts to inflation and exchange rate expectations, and (2) term premia.
Favero and Giavazzi (2002) study the relative importance of each of these factors. According to
this study, policy rates (which are short-term rates) are mostly determined by the first of these
factors, while long term rates are mostly influenced by the second. The current level of the short
rate, though exceptionally high, is the level necessary to stabilize inflation expectations
according to a Taylor-type rule,43 which is remarkable given the absence of formal independence
of the Central Bank.
6.     The situation with long-term    interest rates, however, is different. Putting aside the
fluctuations that occurred in relation to the October 2002 elections, the levels of the Brazilian
term  premia-the main determinants of long-term      rates-reveal market concerns about the
sustainability of the public debt. This hypothesis is supported by two types of evidence, in this
paper: First, we document the existence of a stable relationship by which sovereign spreads and
43 A Taylor rule is a feedback formula designed to guide a central bank in setting short term interest rates as
economic conditions change. The rule determines the short term rate as a function of two arguments: a) the level of
actual inflation relative to the target level; and b) the level of economic activity relative to its potential or full
employment level. If inflation is high relative to its target level, interest rates should go up (and vice versa); also, if
economic activity is high relative to its potential level, interest rates should be raised (and vice versa). It is possible
that inflation is higher than its target level and economic activity is at the same time lower than its target level, or
vice versa, the rule should then provide a firm guideline as to whether interest rates should be raised or lowered See
Taylor ( 1993).
75



ratings are determined jointly by the primary fiscal balance and the public debt level, discussed
later in this annex. And second, we examine preliminary estimates of the term spread, which
show that the main determinants here are volatility and the public debt level (World Bank, 2003).
7.     Negative perceptions regarding the government's solvency create problems for monetary
management, given that the public debt is indexed to short term interest rates and linked with the
dollar. This structure could limit the ability of the Central Bank to let the Real float or to raise
interest rates, creating doubts about the viability of the anti-inflation stance. In this sense, Brazil
could suffer from a subtle form of fiscal dominance.44 To free monetary policy from this
limitation, it is crucial for Brazil to consider lengthening the maturity and duration of public
debt, so that debt mechanics and fiscal policy do not unduly constrain monetary policy.
B. A Sustainable Fiscal Regime
8.     The size and composition of Brazil's public debt contributes to its sovereign risk and
imposes a ceiling on its grade by rating agencies. The total gross domestic and external debt of
the public sector reached 72 percent of GDP by the end of 2002. If hidden liabilities were added
to this figure, estimated at about 10 percent of GDP,45 Brazil's gross debt would exceed 82
percent of GDP, which is the median public debt-to-GDP ratio for B- countries according to
Standard & Poors. B and B+ rated countries have a median public debt ratio of 51 percent of
GDP. Moody's limits for B and B+ ratings (for the debt-to-GDP ratio indicator) range between
71 percent and 54 percent.
9.     In Brazil there is evidence of a positive association between debt levels, sovereign
spreads and domestic interest rates (Kfoury, 2003, World Bank, 2003). Hence, one can
heuristically define an unsustainable fiscal policy as one in which public debt continually rises,
given the principal objective of lowering interest rates. This approach is in accordance with
some analysts' proposals (e.g. see Wyploz, 2002) whereby debt sustainability requires that: (1) at
a minimum, the debt level does not increase; and (2) where the debt is high, a decline in the debt-
to-GDP ratio may be necessary.
10.    According to baseline simulations we performed using an appropriate model for the
purpose, the Brazilian public debt-to-GDP ratio declines when the main determinants of this ratio
(growth, exchange rate, interest rates and spreads) converge to their most likely values without
uncertainty, with the public sector primary surplus remaining constant at 4.25 percent of GDP.
The key results are summarized in Table 1. This baseline scenario assumes that growth
converges to 3.8 percent, which is the potential growth rate of output according to Central Bank
estimates (Teixeira da Silva, 2001). The exchange rate in these simulations depreciates at a rate
equivalent to the difference between domestic and international inflation, starting from the
average forecasted level in 2003 of about 3.5 Reals per dollar.46 Inflation is assumed to decline
44 Tanner and Ramos (2002) examine, statistically, the fiscal dominance argument in Brazil

(2002) and Giacomelli (2002). These figures are not related in any way to the implicit pension debt estimated at
about 300 percent of GDP as estimated in The World Bank, 2001.
46 This is an arbitrary assumption to incorporate the possibility of reversal of the real exchange rate depreciation
experienced in 2002. Since part of the debt accumulation is due to interest payments, which are a flow, these are
valued at the average exchange rate. Stocks are valued at end-of-period exchange rates. Hence the exchange rate
76



slowly to 4 percent annually, while real interest rates converge rapidly to 8 percent per year;
sovereign spreads are assumed to decrease as the debt ratio falls. According to this baseline
scenario, if the public sector primary surplus is maintained at 4.25 percent of GDP, then the net
debt/GDP ratio declines from 57 percent (projected) in 2003 to 50 percent in 2006.47

11.    The above baseline simulation ignores, however, the fact that the Brazilian economy is
subject to random shocks. An increase in volatility can potentially take a country from a path of
sustainable fiscal balances to one that is fiscally unsustainable. If this happens, and if the country
fails to register high enough primary surpluses, the perception that the debt may not be
sustainable will result in higher spreads and make the situation worse. We performed the above
simulations again, this time incorporating uncertainty arising from  the volatility of output,
interest rates and the exchange rate. Under these circumstances, the primary fiscal surplus
required to stabilize the debt-to-GDP ratio is higher than that suggested by the standard
computations, that often ignore the possibility of external shocks.48 The new simulations explain
why, in spite of several years of prudent fiscal policy, the debt-to-GDP ratio in Brazil has not
declined; after all, the country has indeed suffered from adverse external shocks. We now
describe in greater detail how we took external shocks into account in our simulations.
12.    To incorporate uncertainty into the debt sustainability exercise, we performed stress tests
of the debt dynamics. The object of the stress testing exercise is to see how the net public debt
path changes when extreme, but possible, events shock the system. Estimates of the sensitivities
of the debt-to-GDP ratio to changes in each of its determinants were already known at the outset;
but we had to find a way of determining the size of the probable external shocks as reflected by
we use is the mid-point between both, 3 2 Later on we further discuss the assumptions regarding the expected future

unexpected changes in these variables. To do so, we considered the empirical distribution of
each of the variables affecting the trajectory of the debt-to-GDP ratio (real and nominal exchange
rates, real and norninal interest rates, sovereign spreads, and the growth rate of output) and
calculated the sizes of the probable shocks using different levels of confidence.
13.    The stress scenario is based on shocks derived using a 10 percent confidence level, for
most variables;49 the results are given in Table 2. Under this bleak scenario, the exchange rate
would depreciate and lead to higher inflation, under the assumption of a 40 percent pass-through
in the following year.50 The variables were subject to shocks in 2003 and returned to their steady
state level over time, as follows: Growth was assumed to stabilize at about 2 percent rate
annually, and spreads were assumed to not decrease, given that the debt was permanently
increasing. The real interest rate was assumed to remain at 12 percent throughout the simulation
period, and the real exchange rate remained constant after the shock.    In this bleak scenario, a
primary surplus of 4.25 percent of GDP would not be enough to stabilize the debt/GDP ratio; it
would, in fact, cause the debt/GDP ratio to increase significantly. The primary balance that
would stabilize the debt ratio at 53% of GDP over the forecasting horizon is 5.8 percent of GDP.
More specifically, if the primary balance were to be held at an average of 5.8 percent of GDP,
the debt-to-GDP ratio at the end of 2010 would be lower than 53% with a 90 percent
52
probability.  An alternative stress scenario, built around the use of shocks (to the key variables)
derived using a 15 percent confidence level, would require a primary balance of 5.3 percent of
GDP to lead to stabilization of the debt-to-GDP ratio (with an 85 percent probability). Reducing
further the confidence level, so that shocks to the main variables are smaller with a 75 percent
probability (i.e. using a 25 percent confidence level) would imply an average primary surplus of
4.6 percent of GDP to stabilize the debt-to-GDP ratio.
14.    One of the most critical assumptions in the debt sustainability simulations relates to the
path of the real exchange rate. A constant or depreciating real exchange rate scenario requires a
higher primary surplus to stabilize the debt ratio. Examination of the real exchange rate index
since the 1980s shows that in 2002 the real exchange rate index achieved its lowest level in
decades. Whether or not this fact can be interpreted as a low likelihood of having a future
appreciating trend is a matter of debate. If the real exchange rate has a tendency to fluctuate
